On behalf of ILUGC we are constantly looking out for opportunities to
make case for Open source. Some of the events in the last two years
are

1. LDD at MIT
2. LDD at LUCAS TVS
3. Presenation at a Software company Xerago
4. Two day seminar in St.Josesphs Engg College
5. LDD at Asan Memorial School
6. Lecture in Velammal Engg college, RMK Engg college
7. Demo at IEEE

 The problem in organising is in co-ordinating and arranging - i.e
logistics. I request, whoever can, please contact
Colleges/Schools/Corporates and arrange for the seminar/demo or by
whatever name you call it. On behalf of ILUGC we can mobilie
volunteers.

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Wed Dec  1 14:08:20 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar Babu)
Date: Wed Dec  1 14:07:49 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Training on Basics of LINUX
References: <557E17BE74D22143B7BE70EB60E33E9913BE6FFB@shlmsg01.ad.infosys.com>
Message-ID: <cone.1101890300.427176.6208.1000@phobos>

Toufeeq Hussain writes:

> If your really interested in a Training Course in Linux, try STG in
> Mount Road(beside Anand Theatre).
> It has the RHCE course for Rs.10,000

For obvious reasons, it would be a bad idea to suggest the RHCE 
course for a Linux newbie who wants to learn Linux (shell, command-line 
oriented stuff, scripting, utilities, programming and so on) which is a lot 
different from "System Administration". The course fee can also be a 
limiting factor for an enthusiast. Moreover, RHCE courses are tailored to 
churn out "Certified Engineers" (whatever that means) ;-).

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Wed Dec  1 14:45:26 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar Babu)
Date: Wed Dec  1 14:45:07 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Training on Basics of LINUX
References: <557E17BE74D22143B7BE70EB60E33E9913BE6FFD@shlmsg01.ad.infosys.com>
Message-ID: <cone.1101892526.406856.6609.1000@phobos>

Toufeeq Hussain writes:


> No, The STG people tell me that no prior experience is necessary for
> taking the course.

True, most institutes "claim" that fact. But from what I've seen with a lot 
of institutes (no idea about STG though), all they do is teach how to click 
the "Next" button during installation screens, what needs to be entered into 
the text-fields in redhat-config-*, and so on. A newbie would still remain 
clueless about how things work (unless ofcourse he tries out everything on 
his own way). Most institutes align their Linux training *only* to system 
(and/or network) administration. They end up teaching Linux like they would 
teach Novell Netware/UNIX/Windows NT administration. This might _not_ be 
suitable for an enthusiast (who has no interest in becoming a sysadmin). 

That apart, I was baffled to find a couple of RHCE zealots (in bangalore 
atleast) who have no clue about how to add a new service onto a specific 
runlevel, or how to survive without Gnome/KDE or how to write a 2 line 
shell script even! 

> I guess people don't realise that they can learn Linux by themselves and
> join these courses.

Yes, this makes perfect sense. Once people manage to learn Linux by 
themselves, they would never need these courses anyways, unless they have a 
pressing reason, or their company is paying for it ;-)

For the self-learning enthusiast types, google/tldp.org/LUG (as you 
mentioned earlier) are the best bet!  

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

   AFAIK one of the best book u can get to learn linux is "Running
linux" O'Reilly publication. tldp.org has good collection of guides &
HOWTOs. Its greared towards newbies. If u would like to become a core
developer in linux then read hackerhowto ( web-page, search google for
"Hacker howto"). Here hacker means developer. I find
loginataka(web-page) very interesting. It will lead u more quality
books to read. It all depends on how much u r interested. For starting
Runing Linux & tldp.org should do.

ashwin

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Wed Dec  1 17:18:11 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar Babu)
Date: Wed Dec  1 17:17:38 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Training on Basics of LINUX
References: <557E17BE74D22143B7BE70EB60E33E9913BE6FFD@shlmsg01.ad.infosys.com>
	<Pine.LNX.4.58.0412011553440.15023@fileserver.nmsworks.co.in>
Message-ID: <cone.1101901691.171293.8955.1000@phobos>

Kilaru Sambaiah writes:

>   Unix Programming environment

Helps people who have some formal programming/CS background of some sort. I 
wouldn't recommend such a book for a newbie.  

>   Unix sysadmin handbook
>   Principles of Network and sysadmin

Helps people who have some basic exposure to UNIX as a user. 

A Linux enthusiast would also be someone who just bought a new computer 
and wants to try his/her luck on Linux (perhaps after a brief date with 
Windows) and have not much formal CS background. I've managed to find a lot 
of such users lately. Recommending a purely technical book might just 
demotivate them.

Google/TLDP has helped a lot of users to start on with Linux (occasionally 
supplemented with a "For Dummies" kind of book). 


>   google/tldp/LUG only to supplement, not for primary media.
> 
>   How many people are tolerating if some one asks basic question in LUGs?

I hope many do (atleast those who are interested in _helping_ others). In my 
personal experience, this has what set LUGs far apart from the BSD user 
groups and mailing lists back in the 90s. It was _this_ community effort 
that was instrumental in adoption of Linux by non-techie users in 
many ways.

  
Though I do not suggest an absolute newbie to directly expect other 
members of LUG to spoon-feed them, it does make sense for them to be 
involved in LUG (atleast read through the past archives, or search them via 
google) to get enough idea about how to go about solving an installation 
problem or similar commonly raised issues. Of course, like all other 
sensible netizen, a newbie who subscribes to a mailing list must first read 
through the policy docs and act accordingly.   

A search for "Introduction to Linux" on google results in enough excellent 
starting point tutorials on Linux (the first link pointing directly to 
tldp.org). Similarly, there are excellent guides catering to many commonly 
used Linux distributions too.

And yes, learning Linux is a *lot* different from learning Linux System 
Administration (though learning the former lays a firm foundation to 
explore the latter in subject). 

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu

PS: The books that you mentioned are worth the next steep step into 
mastering the subject (Linux/UNIX).

From tharayil at gmail.com  Wed Dec  1 12:53:37 2004
From: tharayil at gmail.com (Tom Tharayil)
Date: Wed Dec  1 18:23:44 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Training on Basics of LINUX
In-Reply-To: <41ADAFEE.1070108@frodo.hserus.net>

>
> bala chandar wrote:
> > Hey,
> > you can say this for other certifications. but for redhat, u need to
> > have talent.and work experience. to solve the issue raised by them
> > during the exam.
>
> that's what they all say, and that's what it is supposed to
> require, at
> least in theory

When I gave the paper it was very interesting...
there was no time to think or even sit down for five minutes.
So I would agree with people who say it was challenging....
not because the questions were unawnserable, but because it was a bit
like the CAT exam.....
leave the candidates for sometime, and they would complete all the
questions, but put them under time stress and you would find out how
many are actually prepared....

One cannot go into the exam unprepared and believing that any issues can
be resolved with a little bit of 'man' or RTFMing on the spot or on the
fly.
That never works out and I can confidently tell you that you wont clear
level1 (which is the easiest of all levels)

A candidate should have ideally prepared for all domains including
sendmail, DNS,samba, wrappers, ftpd, sshd, and so many others which I
cant describe here.
Having said this, a new candidate to Linux would have not be able to
comprehend all the above topics in a matter of just 2 months would he?

He would have to practice and practice and practice....
The examiner cannot help you out much.. Shashi unni is a very busy
man...and dont expect any sort of assistance from anyone there.
Either case RHCE is just an exam to tell the industry that this guy
knows the basics (rather should know the basics) and thats about all.
It saves the recruiters from cross examining the candidate further on
that.

RHCE is certainly not the panacea to all imaginable problems in
Linux/Redhat

The exam itself is 10K and if the course is also another 10k, then I
would seriously think twice.

holy shit....thats 20k straight....

so for newbies.....observe all the threads that go on in ilugc or any
other mailing lists and pay more closer attention when Dr.Sriram replies
to some threads as that went a long way in helping me. Sir, no offense
meant I hope.

http://in.redhat.com/training/rhce/prep_guide.php3

has the prep guide to the RHCE...

atb

regards
Tom

bala chandar writes:

> I have designed the home page of ilugc to change the existing
> website(www.chennailug.org).

The design looks simple and neat. Here are my suggestions though:

1. The ILUGC logo found on existing site looks cool, and it also 
provides the site (and also the group) a form of unique identity! We call 
it "branding" in corporate/marketing jargon. I think we must retain it (or 
improve upon it). 

2. The powered-by logos are a bit out-of-place. Perhaps they are 
better at the bottom of the page (away from the mouse hover zones).  
The existing site seems to have them at the right place.

3. The search field looks better if moved to the topmost right corner of the 
header. 

The current site is based on HTML 4.01 standard. We could have our new site 
(if at all) using current standards like XHTML 1.0 (or 1.1) with all layout 
information moved to CSS.

Anyways, keep up the great work ;-)

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.


PS: One site that I was impressed by their design/usability/user-experience 
lately - http://www.xaraya.com/. There are many others though.

"Bharath.G" <g.bharath@gmail.com> wrote:
> box ends up being just another linux solution , even mobile phones
> now-a-days are equipped with a similar configuration for almost the
> same price.But it is really nice to hear about your new effort to
> spread linux usage.

yeah - mobile phones, small "wifi router + firewall in a box" type stuff
such
as the linksys wrt54g etc all exist, and it is nice seeing linux ported to
various embedded platforms.

but please consider what differentiates your port from all the rest of the
linux ports out there .. you will need to focus on the actual userspace apps
/
kernel features you'll have to include for your product, and see about
porting
those as well .. and whether it is worth writing a whole new port, or just
concentrating on porting and optimizing various apps to an existing embedded
platform for your new app.

	srs

From sridharinfinity at gmail.com  Thu Dec  2 07:56:17 2004
From: sridharinfinity at gmail.com (Sridhar R)
Date: Thu Dec  2 07:56:24 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Ilugc Wiki Guidelines
Message-ID: <8816fcf80412011826590797d7@mail.gmail.com>

Hello all,

Ilugc wiki is here
http://www.chennailug.org/wiki/

If you don't know what a wiki is read here
http://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/wiki

Just click on the 'edit this page' link of any page and help on the
format used for editing wiki pages is here
http://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/How_to_edit_a_page

To start new pages, either
1. Open the URL directly -
http://www.chennailug.org/wiki/index.php/My_New_Page and refer the URL
to some index page
2. (Or) put the page link in index page [[My New Page]] and click on the link

Read mediawiki docs for more information

And don't forget to create a separate user account for yourselves.

As anyone can edit, any evil mind can do mishap, but since mediawiki
is version controlled, we can always revert the changes ('history'
link of that page or Recent:Changes).  To monitor the changes everyone
should have a look at
http://www.chennailug.org/wiki/index.php/Special:Recentchanges


-- 
Sridhar R - http://cs.annauniv.edu/~rsridhar
Blog: http://www.livejournal.com/~sridharinfinity

Sridhar R writes:

> What about using Drupal?
> http://drupal.org

I personally would suggest a CMS [Drupal/Plone/Etomite/Xaraya] for the 
website. Administration is easy, and they also come with a lot of
goodies (Tracking hits/Referres/Statistics/Advanced User Management/so on). 
A website can easily carry a more professional look if based on a good 
CMS.

I guess wikis are best used as community-driven knowledge management 
software rather than being used as website deployment tools.

Chandrashekar Babu.

'submit' their content rather than editing it we could have some CMS
like drupal.

--- GMail <shekhaar@gmail.com> wrote:
> Is there any tools !! which modifies the make file
> for 2.4 to port it to 2.6 ?

It depends on what variables you use in the Makefile.
I only use this in a Makefile for a 2.6 module:

obj-m := driver.o

and compile using:

#make -C /usr/src/linux SUBDIRS=$PWD modules

Subject: [Ilugc] copyright period

Hi,

Copyright notices usually are of the format:
Copyright <period> <copyright holder>

Like, from linux/kernel/fork.c :

/*
 *  linux/kernel/fork.c
 *
 *  Copyright (C) 1991, 1992  Linus Torvalds
 */

What does the period suggest and how is it decided ? 
In the above example, what happens after 1992 ? 

saha

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Thu Dec  2 14:50:04 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar Babu)
Date: Thu Dec  2 14:49:29 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: copyright period
References: <614380C6B0E7AC498D4DAE964E2F553DD8C9E2@chatgavsin.com>
Message-ID: <cone.1101979204.822164.6906.1000@phobos>

Anand Kumar Saha writes:


> /*
>  *  linux/kernel/fork.c
>  *
>  *  Copyright (C) 1991, 1992  Linus Torvalds
>  */
> 
> What does the period suggest and how is it decided ? 
> In the above example, what happens after 1992 ? 


The period suggests the year(s) when the original work was 
created and/or published. The entire work remains copyrighted for 
atleast 25-50 years from the year(s) as mentioned on the notice. 

The website http://www.whatiscopyright.org/ should clarify most of your 
doubts relevant to copyright notices.


Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu

Have a look at drupal's features for eg.
http://drupal.org/features

Many CMS's are extensible.  Drupal has 'modules'.  If you need any
specific (to ilugc) functionality you could always create a drupal
module and plug it up.
Look at the modules written for drupal here
http://drupal.org/project/releases

I think it makes perfect sense to bring drupal for ilugc website.  It
does have user management, which means collaborative editing is
possible.

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Thu Dec  2 20:06:52 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar Babu)
Date: Thu Dec  2 20:06:14 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Disk Quota service for Samba
References: <20041202094752.91833.qmail@web41729.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <cone.1101998212.462618.11315.1000@phobos>

Anandh G writes:

> I had setup a DC server using samba in FC 2. I have
> all users to have their home directory stored in the
> server. I want to implement quota service for all
> users home directory individually. I have criteria
> like to have a maximum of 50MB for some users, 200MB
> for some, etc.

One method that I can think of, is by creating two new groups - one for 
users who need 200 MB of usage space and another for the set of users who 
need 50 MB of disk usage space on /home directory. Then, by using quota 
relevant tools (edquota, quotaon), you should be able to set disk usage 
constraints for these groups on /home directory. Depending on which group 
the user belongs to, he should be able to inherit constraints as set on the 
group.

I haven't tried this method practically, but I hope it should solve 
the issue.

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu

Hi,
I found some q&a reg. RH 3.0 update at the following url
http://forums1.itrc.hp.com/service/forums/questionanswer.do?admit=716493758+1102051002447+28353475&threadId=733502

out of which i have picked up one answer which might help you:

SteveLitzkow  Nov 17, 2004 13:35:36 GMT    unassigned   
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
I found the update on the distribution media.
It was on disc #1 in the folder /RedHat/Updates/

I guess we purchased RedHat long after its initial release. So Red Hat
just put the update in with the media.

Our application was getting this error until we applied the Update:
error while loading shared libraries: libstdc++-libc6.2-2.so.3: cannot
open shared object file: No such file or directory

cheers!

From ajosephantony at yahoo.co.in  Fri Dec  3 04:42:45 2004
From: ajosephantony at yahoo.co.in (Joseph Antony)
Date: Fri Dec  3 18:12:57 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] problem:with cli(), sti() 
In-Reply-To: <20041203102524.65222.qmail@web8405.mail.in.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20041203124245.20933.qmail@web8403.mail.in.yahoo.com>

Hi,

Did you include "linux/sched.h" ??
Also, usage of sti()is not recommended. Instead use
save_flags and cli during disabling and restore_flags
during enabling.

Using sti may be hazardous in the sense that your
process does not take into consideration all the
changes that has happened between cli() and sti()
calls. Hence, it may hamper/destablise another
process. Restoring flags just ORs data related to your
process only. 

Hope this helps.

Cheers,
Joseph

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Fri Dec  3 10:49:16 2004
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Sat Dec  4 00:19:29 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] problem:with cli(), sti() 
In-Reply-To: <20041203102524.65222.qmail@web8405.mail.in.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20041203184916.36764.qmail@web50207.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi,

> i used cli() & sti() function's  to disabling 
> interrupt's(as per Linux device driver book of
> O'Relly)

Which version of the book? cli() and sti() are old
usage styles. You are to use spin_lock functions
instead.

Which header files did you include? Make sure you
don't have these set in your kernel:

<> Prompt for development and/or incomplete
code/drivers
<> Set version information on all module symbols

Regards,

K Shakthi

Date: Sat Dec  4 00:22:55 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] kernel programming
In-Reply-To: <20041203112641.41560.qmail@web51806.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi,

--- simi mathur <simi_mathur1@yahoo.com> wrote:
> Is there any kernel internals/programming classes in
> chennai?

What prevents you from learning on your own? An old P2
machine with 32 MB RAM is more than enough to do
kernel programming.

You need to get recognition from the open source
community that you are a competitive programmer and
that you can contribute to the community. No institute
(atleast that I know of) teaches you that. The more
you interact with the community and provide valuable
contributions, the better. This should give you a
start:

http://www.kernelnewbies.org

Good luck,

K Shakthi

You can use:

dpkg-reconfigure xserver-xfree86

The settings are saved here (and you can edit by hand):

/etc/X11/XF86Config-4

From igni_linux at yahoo.com  Sat Dec  4 19:00:23 2004
From: igni_linux at yahoo.com (ignacius nallu)
Date: Sun Dec  5 08:30:34 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Detailed explanation on the PROCESS OF REPOSITORY
	CONVERSION FROM VSS TO CVS
Message-ID: <20041205030023.98293.qmail@web54103.mail.yahoo.com>

Dear all,
This is how I converted from VSS to CVS in our
company.The softwares that we use are pure OSS. I am
striving to thrush Linux using in our company.


PROCESS OF REPOSITORY CONVERSION FROM VSS TO CVS:

1.Deleted all previous test sandboxes of all the
existing PCs by searching for folder workace and find
whether it is a cvs folder that too in directories
created for each user.
2.Logged in as root and deleted previous repository
folders in the linux server Red hat linux9 hosted as
cvs server.
3.Logged in as a cvs user[cvs group user] and
Initialised the cvs repository from scratch [ folder
permissions, etc.,]
Administrative setup:
Added binary files list to cvswrappers file - By
checking what all binary files are used in our
PROJECTMODULE
CVSROOT/notify file edited for sending mails during
watches 
CVSROOT/users file added to repository
CVSROOT/checkoutlist file editing and adding users
file to it.usernames and mail ids added to
CVSROOT/users file.
copied contrib.pl to $CVSROOT/CVSROOT directory for
sending commit logs
edited CVSROOT/loginfo file for commit logs as mail to
administrators
Ran vss2cvs.pl from a windows PC in LAN as per the
readme provided with vss2perl.pl set of
scripts.Completed successfully.
logged in as cvs user[cvs group user] and ran
massage.pl on folder PROJECTMODULE-Completed
successfully.This is to remove fake timestamps.
Backedup repository in each stage...
And ofcourse the cvs repository can be resynched with
the VSS repository
And thats the whole process.Anybody of you having
doubts regarding version control please feel free ask
me,

ENJOY THE SPIRIT OF GNU/OSS

thank you
Ignacius

From rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au  Mon Dec  6 00:22:45 2004
From: rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au (Raja Subramanian)
Date: Mon Dec  6 00:26:51 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] GeeXBoX - a standalone media player
Message-ID: <20041205185245.GA28358@pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au>


Hi,

Check out the GeeXBoX project at -
    http://www.geexbox.org/en/index.html

It's a live CD that contains mplayer and friends.
The current 0.98 release is measly 6MB ISO and can play -

  1. mpg 1/2 movies - mpg files, VCDs, DVDs.
  2. mpg 4 - DivX.
  3. realmedia, winmedia, mp3, oog, audio streams, etc.

If you have TV-out on your PC, then you can watch your videos
on the tele.  It also supports joysticks and some remotes.

I hope we can now play The Revolution OS and The Code on
special occasions without much trouble :-)

- Raja

References: <001101c4db36$ffb0a4a0$41a841db@i0r1b2>

Hi,

> GDM: X server not found !
> Error: command could not be executed.
> Please install X server or edit /etc/gdm.conf to point

> Usually XF86Config file is placed in /etc/X11 dir. But in Sarge
> it was not seen.
 
> Initially it starts off from .Xauthority file, but after
> the error, I see that the file is having 0 bytes.
 
> Here also startx will not make x work with error msg
> /usr/lib/X11R6/bin/xinit/xiniitrc - No such file or directory

All the above four messages indicate that you have not installed the
xserver packages properly. Did you try installing the
"x-window-system" pseudo package which takes care of installing the
Xserver and few basic X clients?

$ dpkg -l | grep "X Window" 

will give you information on what are the X Window system packages
that are currently installed on your machine.

Cheers,
Natarajan

I used the 2.6 kernel and X started without a problem.
I selected Desktop Environment in the Debian Installer and it
automatically installed XFree86/GNOME/KDE.

I used "vesa" driver and pretty toned down Monitor Settings.

After you get X to work, make a backup of the XFree86-4 file and then
start tweaking the settings.

Do so until you get the desired ones.

Hi,

Balaji G wrote:
> I would like to know whether Red Hat 7. 2 which runs a 2.4.X kernel
> supports 160 GB of Space coz when i installed it in my office it  just
> took 130 GB but didnt recognize the remaining 30 GB. Should i tweak
> anything so that it takes 160 GB or should i move on to a recent
> version of Linux ?

It's not the software that's the problem.  Its your hardware - your HDD
controller needs to support 48bit LBA.  IIRC, most ata/133 controllers
suppor disks > 137GB.  Look for "137GB ata" on google for solutions.

- Raja

From kums at gmx.net  Mon Dec  6 23:41:01 2004
From: kums at gmx.net (Kumaraguru)

Subject: [Ilugc] Re: ilugc Digest, Vol 7, Issue 20
References: <OF1FC767B2.CD151FE0-ON65256F62.004C2874@polaris.co.in>
Message-ID: <005801c4dbbe$f3610ef0$0d07a8c0@kums>

Hi Mahesh,

A few months ago,while I was using PCQ Linux 2004(based on Fedora)
I bought a Dax Smartlink Internal Modem card (PCTEL chipset).
The supplied driver cd only had a binary module compiled for
some 2.2.x kernel and I tried everywhere to get the driver for
my 2.4 kernel.

Even the unoffical ones
http://linmodems.technion.ac.il/pctel-linux/welcome.html
were not helpful for this particular chipset. Thankfully, I had
my old 33.6Kbps External modem which comfortably works under
linux.

The problem could have been avoided if Modem Chipset makers
provide source code of their drivers or at least update
their binaries for new kernel releases.

I suggest you buy an External modem or carefully pick an
Internal Modem that's well supported under linux...or
You could do yourself a favour and switch to a broadband
service(FYI: I subscribe to Hathway's Cable Internet
service that doesn't require any modem at all and works
quite well under Linux)

Regards
Kumaraguru

An excerpt from Release notes of FC3 may be of use for you
------------------------------------------------------------

In order to eliminate the redundancy inherent in providing a separate
package for the kernel source code when that source code already
exists in the kernel's .src.rpm file, Fedora Core 3 no longer includes
the kernel-source package. Users that require access to the kernel
sources can find them in the kernel .src.rpm file. To create an
exploded source tree from this file, perform the following steps (note
that <version> refers to the version specification for your
currently-running kernel):

Obtain the kernel-<version>.src.rpm file from one of the following sources:

The SRPMS directory on the appropriate "SRPMS" CD iso image

The FTP site where you got the kernel package

By running the following command:

up2date --get-source kernel

Install kernel-<version>.src.rpm (given the default RPM configuration,
the files this package contains will be written to /usr/src/redhat/)

Change directory to /usr/src/redhat/SPECS/, and issue the following command:

rpmbuild -bp --target=<arch> kernel.spec

(Where <arch> is the desired target architecture.)

On a default RPM configuration, the kernel tree will be located in
/usr/src/redhat/BUILD/.

In resulting tree, the configurations for the specific kernels shipped
in Fedora Core 3 are in the /configs/ directory. For example, the i686
SMP configuration file is named
/configs/kernel-<version>-i686-smp.config. Issue the following command
to place the desired configuration file in the proper place for
building:

cp <desired-file> ./.config

Issue the following command:

make oldconfig

You can then proceed as usual.

From linux at frodo.hserus.net  Tue Dec  7 12:35:21 2004
From: linux at frodo.hserus.net (Suresh Ramasubramanian)
Date: Tue Dec  7 12:35:36 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: [LIH]qmail+smtp auth+vpopmail
In-Reply-To: <1cc2ae104120622521d7c140@mail.gmail.com>
References: <1cc2ae104120622521d7c140@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <41B55631.2020905@frodo.hserus.net>

Narayanamoorthy Srinivasan wrote:
>    I installed qmail+vpopmail+smtp auth. For SMTP auth i am using
> vchkpw of vpopmail for authentication. All are working fine. Able to
> send mails using smpt auth.
>   But there are no logs to check who send the message. Maillog shows
> just the mails send - from ID and to ID. Is there anyway to get the
> username/password by which mail was sent./

Ise tjos tp start qmail-smtpd-chkusr - assuming you're using 
http://www.interazioni.it/opensource/chkusr/

#!/bin/sh -e
#
# Using splogger to send the log through syslog.

exec env - PATH="/var/qmail/bin:/usr/local/bin" \
tcpserver -t 5 -v -p -x <your.tcp.smtp.cdb> \
-u <vpopmail-user> -g <vchkpw-group> -l <your-host.domain> 0 smtp \
qmail-smtpd-chkusr splogger smtpd &

	srs

From: "Natarajan K" <knutties@gmail.com>
> All the above four messages indicate that you have not installed the

> that are currently installed on your machine.

>

Hi
I got some more clue from comp.os.linux newsgroup which gave a tip to give
PS2 mouse protocol as ImPS/2 if I start installing with 2.6 kernel. Now X is
working
----------------------

"Bob Hauck" <postmaster@localhost.localdomain> wrote in message
> I have four machines running 2.6 kernels with X.  There was a change
> between 2.4 and 2.6 regarding the mouse.  2.6 uses /dev/input/mice for
> all mice, and the protocol is always ImPS/2 because the kernel will
> translate if that isn't what you have.  If the mouse is not set up right
> then X will not start with a message about "no core pointer".
>
> I don't remember if I ran into that on any of these machines, all but
> one of them was upgraded from 2.4 to 2.6 so I fixed XF86Config by hand
> before doing the upgrade.
>
>
> --
>  -| Bob Hauck
>  -| To Whom You Are Speaking
>  -| http://www.haucks.org/

Yes, this worked !
This time I gave mouse protocol as ImPS/2 nad the X server is installed and
working perfectly!
Previously I gave it as Plain PS/2 and the X did not get installed (which I
did not fully grasp the first time) and apt-get install xserver-xfree86
later also failed because of this during the subsequent installation trials.
Thanks once again!
Srikanth
----------------------------------------------

Srikanth


From lug at chandrashekar.info  Tue Dec  7 18:33:46 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar Babu)
Date: Tue Dec  7 18:32:58 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Problems in using Logitech Mouse in Linux
References: <92ac7fad0412062200322f4b7f@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <cone.1102424626.44981.2587.1000@phobos>

Rajesh Kumar writes:


> 1. Mouse configuration. I'm having a Logitech mouse, but my Linux
> identifies it as Generic Mouse (PS/2).I tried it changing using
> mouseconfig command at terminal but it leads me to non-working of the
> mouse.Moreover with this Generic type I couldn't use my scroll
> button.

I presume that your problem is relevant to mouse scroll-wheel support on X 
Window System.
Depending on your distro, check if either /etc/X11/XF86Config-4 or 
/etc/X11/xorg.conf file exists, open the file using a text editor of your 
choice and search for the mouse section block which resembles the following:

Section "InputDevice"
   Identifier "Mouse1"
   ...
EndSection

Within this block, make sure that you have the following line (before 
"EndSection"):
    Option "ZAxisMapping"       "4 5"

Also make sure that you have the line as follows (somewhere in the 
beginning of the section):
     Option "Protocol" "Auto"

-or-
    Option "Protocol" "ImPS/2"

 
> 2. Believe me but its true. MY LINUX HANGS !! I'm using elx linux with
> kernel 2.4.x which is said to be the stable,but whenever I was
> connected to internnet(dialup-BSNL) my system hangs after exactly 45
> mins. I couldn't figure out the problem.Please help me.

This has to do with either your hardware, or support for your hardware 
by the Linux distribution itself. I haven't used elx, so cannot comment 
about its stability. If the problem persists  with other linux  
distributions too, this can be also hardware problem. Try another 
(better) distro (like Slackware/Debian/Mandrake/SuSE/Knoppix) and let us 
know.

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

v.0.44"
Gnu \Gnu\, n. [Hottentot gnu, or nju: cf. F. gnou.] (Zo["o]l.)
One of two species of large South African antelopes of the
genus Catoblephas, having a mane and bushy tail, and curved
horns in both sexes. [Written also gnoo.]
[1913 Webster]

                      Try this command  to find the process which is 
using that device. mostly it will work.

$lsof | grep /home/user1/mnt/

Bharathi Raja.

From ramanraj at vsnl.com  Wed Dec  8 16:56:06 2004

Subject: [Ilugc] ILUGC LOGO

  Toufeeq Hussain wrote:

>Heh heh :D
>
>It is a cow right ?
>
>I meant no disrespect to the logo.
>
>Just that I feel it needs representation too in the ILUGC logo.
>
*Undocumented incident that happened during ILUGC Install Fest 2004*

I was wearing a black coloured t-shirt with a GNU head logo printed on 
the front pocket.  A gentleman came up to me and asked why I have 
dressed up "inauspiciously" - with "Lord Yama's vahana", pointing to the 
GNU head :)  I said it is a Gnu, an African antelope, a symbol for the 
GNU project, and indeed it also looks like Lord Yama's vahana because it 
spells doom for proprietary software ;)  But as Toufeeq Hussain rightly 
points, the GNU head also looks very similar to a cow, albeit like 
Kamadhenu, giving as much as we can ask for. Etienne Suvasa, is believed 
to be the artist of the GNU logo.

The Penguin is already the logo for Linux, and the Gnu head is a logo 
for the Gnu Project. Ideally, a logo for an org should be a unique 
symbol not imitating any pre-existing logos that are well associated 
with other orgs.   I would suggest a golden spotted Deer [head] symbol 
for ILUGC.  Most of the ILUGC meetings are at IIT-M, and the sighting of 
deer while driving towards the meeting venue is one of the additional 
pleasures provided by ILUGC meets.  It would be an "I-like-see deer" 
also ;) The Deer could also be used as a mark on any custom distros that 
ILUGC may create in the future. It is up to the graphic artist to make 
the deer look like both the gnu head, and the penguin too, using some 
morphing tool, or the logo section would end up looking like a mini zoo 
;) Other logos may also suit ILUGC, if any change in the existing scheme 
is seen fit.

My linuxrc file (which is in initrd img ) is this file.

####################################################
#!/bin/nash

echo Mounting /proc filesystem
mount -t proc /proc /proc
echo Creating block devices
mkdevices /dev
echo Creating root device
mkrootdev /dev/root
echo 0x0100 > /proc/sys/kernel/real-root-dev
echo Mounting root filesystem
mount -o defaults --ro -t ext3 /dev/root /sysroot
pivot_root /sysroot /sysroot/initrd
umount /initrd/proc
####################################################

I wanna know wht is implied by /sysroot.

whether it means "root(hd0,0)" which i have given in /boot/grub/menu.lst

On my machine (AMD AthlonXP 1800+, 256MB RAM, KT266 chipset, GeForce2/MX

quality is excellent on 5.1 channels. Same goes for the video quality too

DVD drive) for Windows 2000 had issues playing the video using true-color. 
Anyways, I dont have Windows anymore, so cant comment much about it. But on 
linux, both sound and video have been great for my machine configuration.

From raamanp at yahoo.co.in  Thu Dec  9 06:04:15 2004
From: raamanp at yahoo.co.in (Raman.P)
Date: Thu Dec  9 11:34:22 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT] exporting shell variable - perl
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.58.0412082323290.26558@chi.spunge.org>
Message-ID: <20041209060415.2515.qmail@web8502.mail.in.yahoo.com>

 --- carti <carti@chi.spunge.org> wrote: 
> Hi,
> 
> I am able to export a variable to my shell through shell
> program(korn shell).
> 
> When I tried to do exporting variable in perl program
> using system command. It is not working.
> The snippet of my code is as follows.
> 
> system("export
>
SHLIB_PATH=/base/content/matlab/bin/hpux:/base/content/matlab/extern/lib/hpux");
> 
> So, presently, I am forced to give the export in the shell
> in command line and then run the perl program.
> 
> Is there anyway in perl to export the shell variable.
> 
> Trying for sometime in Google does not give me good pointers.

When you use system the environment changes affects only that
command.

You can manipulate environment using perl special variable $ENV
for example
$dsquery=$ENV{'DSQUERY'};
printf "before dsquery=$dsquery\n";
$ENV{'DSQUERY'}='querynew';
$dsquery=$ENV{'DSQUERY'};
printf "after dsquery=$dsquery\n";

Raman.P

Subject: [Ilugc] Suggestion to Promote Linux

Hi,

Presently, in Linux I find lot of utilities
which are not there in Windows. Because of this
advantage I started using Linux(long time back),
and this gave me an edge over others(non Linuxers)
in all places.

Though there are lot(numerous) utilities, only a
few are mostly used my most people most of the times.
To name a few, editiors vi, emacs, shell scripting,
commands(both user level and admin level), configuration,
perl coding, python coding, apache, mysql, etc.

Though there are good number of good sites on any of these
above topics, there can never be one good site which is the
consolidation of all sites(For example sites for vi editor).

I am sure there are quite a lot of ilugc members who are
good in many of these topics(utilities). Our members know
many things which others do not know. Why not create a
documentation (OR) guide (OR) tutorial (OR) TIPS & TRICKS
sort of thing which will HELP beginners and which can
HELP others who know better and interested to CONTRIBUTE.

I think Time is not going to be a constraint as nobody
is forced to do. If anyone is willing to share any TIP
or guide he will just contribute.

Basically a knowledge repository will be great for
ilugc members.

I think this would be a good pointer to think about.

Keep pouring your ideas.

Thanks and Regs,
carti

From kums at gmx.net  Thu Dec  9 12:06:40 2004
From: kums at gmx.net (Kumaraguru)
Date: Thu Dec  9 12:08:15 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: ilugc Digest, Vol 7, Issue 23
In-Reply-To: <OFAB2545F0.55610FC4-ON65256F65.001782A8@polaris.co.in>

Message-ID: <1102574201.12532.8.camel@kums.kumsdom>

Hi Mahesh,

http://www.redhat.com/magazine/001nov04/features/fedoracore3/
says..

************************************************************************
Fedora Core 3 no longer includes the kernel-source package. Users who
want to rebuild the kernel are encourage to download the kernel-
<version>.src.rpm source RPM, install it, and build kernel-source from
it. However, if a user wants to build a module against the existing
kernel, the entire kernel source tree is not required.
Refer to the Release Notes for details on both these operations.

************************************************************************

The release note:
http://fedora.redhat.com/docs/release-notes/fc3/x86/  says

************************************************************************
An exploded source tree is not required to build kernel modules against
the currently in-use kernel.

For example, to build the foo.ko module, create the following file
(named Makefile) in the directory containing the foo.c file:


obj-m    := foo.o

KDIR    := /lib/modules/$(shell uname -r)/build
PWD    := $(shell pwd)

default:
    $(MAKE) -C $(KDIR) SUBDIRS=$(PWD) modules
          

Issue the make command to build the foo.ko module.

************************************************************************


Regards
Kumaraguru

On Thu, 09 Dec 2004 05:53:05 -0800, T.K.Venu Gopal
<v27076685@fastmail.fm> wrote:
> hi to all
> 
> i want to known weather am running lilo or grub
> on my system console, how?
> (not while booting after boot / dmesg ).
> 

For grub, try this
$ grep "Loading stage" /dev/hda

If you get "Binary file matches" pretty quick, then grub is installed,
otherwise ctrl+c ... and try for the corresponding string for lilo.

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Thu Dec  9 06:19:46 2004
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Thu Dec  9 19:49:56 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] problem:with cli(), sti() 
In-Reply-To: <20041209103923.22214.qmail@web8405.mail.in.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20041209141946.87351.qmail@web50207.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi Madhukar,

--- Madhukar mythri <madhukar_linux@yahoo.co.in>
wrote:
> my_lock is declared as Global variable of type
> spinlock_t..
> and assigned "SPIN_LOCK_UNLOCKED"
>  
> is what i did was correct???

If you are accessing the variable among different
functions it has to be declared global. Usually, you
lock a particular variable instance (maybe in a data
structure) that is susceptible to a race condition.
Are you working on a SMP system?

You also don't want to do too much stuff between
locking and unlocking it. Remember, you are disabling
interrupts for the processor. The best way is to do
the needful and transfer the rest of the work to
bottom halves.

I would encourage you to read the spinlock section
here:

http://www.xml.com/ldd/chapter/book/ch09.html

Also check Chapter 4. Interrupts and Exceptions in
"Understanding the Linux Kernel" by Daniel P. Bovet,
and Marco Cesati. 

http://www.oreilly.com/catalog/linuxkernel/toc.html

> hey, do u know tomarrow Their is a Linux Festival in
> Taj hotel conducting by IBM people.???
> Did u register??

I believe it is on IBM web portals and application
stuff on GNU/Linux. I spend most of time living in
kernel-space, so it won't be of much use to me. Thanks
anyway.

Have fun,

K Shakthi

Hi all,

I was a passive member of this group for last couple of months ( i did
attend one of the ilugc meetings though), but on reading this thread i
thought there was a need to express mine..

       The Computer users all over the world has developed a trend
that a google search will get you every thing.. but i think its not
the case always. What google show is the matches of the keyword you
have given... It doesn't make a content based evaluation or in simple
terms doesn't ensure the quality of the content that is found in the
results.

       Suppose i am a newbie to linux and want to know about
programming on linux environment ; a search for "linux programming"
will retrieve you 13,600,000 results ... Here i am sure it will take
him weeks to understand what python is used for and what php is used
for ....

       Now , how we can help the community is.... 
          a) List down all your favourite  sites 
          b) Classify them based on  "what it talks about?" and  "how
it helped you?"
    
      and mind you, these classifications should be checked for
content not category.

    This list can be put up in the new ilugc wiki site under different
categories with a neat briefing of what each link is for ...

   I am absolutely percent sure that your Favourites list (or
Bookmarks) will help hundreds like you.....

Looking forward to hear a lot more about this from all of you..

regards,
Praveen.P.V

Subject: [Ilugc] problem:with cli(), sti()

Hi Madhukar,

> will it disable  interrupt's of all process runing
> in
> system??? 
> "or"  just disable the current process interrupt???

Interrupts are for the _processor_ and the system. You
will be able to see all the interrupts assigned in the
output of "cat /proc/interrupts". Similarily, you will
also find useful info from the output of "cat
/proc/stat". Interrupts could be from external
peripherals or system interrupts (timer, for example).
 
> save_flags()..
> cli()
> /*...code with disabling interrrupt's..**/
> restore_flags();
> 
> is it??

Yes. Check this:
http://lxr.linux.no/source/include/linux/spinlock.h#L10

> and spin_lock_irqsave() is better effiency than
> this...i hope....

Yes, it is.

MEDIA LAB ASIA. Empanelment of consultants and organisations for
design, development, prototyping, system integration and test
deployment of ICT systems in rural areas.

Media Lab Asia has been set up by the Ministry of Communications and
Information Technology, Government of India to research, develop and
deploy ICT and other technologies for the benefit of commonman.

To successfully implement this programme, Media Lab Asia intends to
enter into project-based collaborations with different solution
providers in their areas of expertise.

For this purpose, Media Lab Asia invites applications for empanelment
of consultants and organisations who have interest, ideas, skills and
experience to participate by way of identification, research, design,
development, prototyping, system integration and field deployment of
ICT systems in rural areas.

ILLUSTRATIVE AREAS OF WORK

* Broadband wireless communication technologies and products.
* Low cost access devices
* ICT for healthcare
   - Low cost & ICT integrated/enabled medical equipment for
     primary healthcare.
   - Healthcare information and management systems.
   - Telemedicine tools and devices
   - Field data collection devices, tools and software.
* ICT in education
   - Multimedia educational content development tools in local
     languages and English
   - Educational content in local languages and English
   - Virtual laboratory experiments, etc
* ICT tools to enhance livelihood
   - Rural e-commerce tools
   - Tools for rural interaction and information exchange
* Advanced multi-nodal interfaces and local languages
* Assistive devices and technologies for disabled.

For details and empanelment information, long on to

 	http://www.medialabasia.org.in

Apply within 15 days to: Officer on Special Duty (OSD), Media Lab Asia, 
4th Floor,  Samruddhi Venture Park, Central MIDC Road, Andheri (East), 
Mumbai - 400093. Tel +22-2831 2930 or 2831 2931 Fax +22 283 79158

Subject: [Ilugc] getmail/ Procmail problem
Message-ID: <20041210085258.57138.qmail@web41723.mail.yahoo.com>

I am having a mail server x.com at my ISP, which will
collect the mails for any user to postmaster@x.com. At
my client place I will fetch it from x.com and store
it in mailroot mailbox locally and then distribute it
to all other local users. I was using fetchmail with
procmail to do this. and it is working well, but I
want to migrate from fetchmail to getmail. At this
time the mail is retrived by getmail and stored in
mailroot, but procmail is not distributing the mails
to other users.
The following are the configs

Getmail Version 4
=====================
/root/.getmail/getmailrc
[retriever]
type = SimplePOP3Retriever
server = mail.x.com
username = postmaster@x.com
password = xxx
                                                      
                         
[destination]
user = mailroot
type = Mboxrd
path = /var/spool/mail/mailroot

Fetch mail V 6.2
====================================
/root/,fetchmail
poll mail.ideafarms.com proto pop3
user "postmaster@x.com" pass "xxx" is mailroot

Procmail 3.22
===================================
~/mailroot/.procmail
:0
* ^(To|Cc|Bcc):.*a.b@x.com
!ab
:0
* ^(To|Cc|Bcc):.*c.d@x.com
!cd

Plz reply me! Urgent

=====
Regards,
AnandhG

No, getmail needs procmail to distribute mails to
local users, as it is getting from postmaster@x.com. 
I somehow managed to set getmail to work with procmail
by using this config.

[destination]
type = MDA_external
path = /usr/bin/procmail
arguments = ('/home/mailroot/.procmailrc',)
user = mailroot

The mails are distributing to the local users
perfectly. But there is one problem with procmail. My
procmail config is
:0
* ^(To|Cc|Bcc):.*ban.sh@x.com
!ban
:0
* ^(To|Cc|Bcc):.*vij.g@x.com
!vijay

If a mail which is destined To: vij.g@x.com and cc:
ban.sh@x.com, that mail is only delivered to ban user,
the other rule (for vij.g@x.com) is not checking. If I
swaped both the entries, to be vij.g first & ban.sh
second. That mail is delivered only to vijay and not
to ban. 

How should I make procmail to go thru all the rules
before exiting.



=====
Regards,
AnandhG

colleges,public fests etc.

demo/seminar/lecture or by whatever name you want to call - it in
your college/corporates or any suitable place and ILUGC will arrange
for technical volunteers.

Mandrake 10.0 official Powerpack CD6
(Mandrakelinux10.0-Official-Powerpack-CD6.i586.iso)

contains only trial or limited demo versions of
commerical applications like ..

Antivirus Applications(Bitdefender,Drweb,Kaspersky..),
Virtualization Software(VMWare..),
Windows Emulators like (Code Weavers, Win4Lin)
CAD software(VariCAD)
Video Editing Software(MainActor) etc..

The complete list is here..
http://www.mandrakesoft.com/products/10/isv

AFAIK, these are not legally redistributable.
Generally speaking..they are not at all essential!

Kumaraguru

From topa_007 at yahoo.com  Sat Dec 11 05:37:29 2004
From: topa_007 at yahoo.com (Toufeeq)
Date: Sat Dec 11 19:07:37 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Minutes of the Meet 11-Dec-2004
Message-ID: <20041211133729.24922.qmail@web12702.mail.yahoo.com>

Venue: ADI Tenet Seminar Hall,IIT M
Time :1500 Hrs

The meet started off late at around 1530 hrs , by that
time a crowd of around 20 had arrived.
Srinivas started the meet with a report about Linux
Bangalore 2004. He mentioned the talks, the speakers
and the quality of the talks/seminars held during
LB2004. Saravanan also gave his inputs on the
subjects.
Srini, further mentioned the content of these talks
and how they varied from kernel level to the GNU
philosophy.

After the brief discussion on LB2004, Raman started
his session on Shell Scripting for Newbies.
Raman gave a brief introduction about the variables,
their declaration and their usage.
Small code snippets were also presented. Usage of
common utilities like echo,ls, cut,wc was explained.
Then followed an explanation on the programming
constructs that make up Shell Scripting.
The various loops , for, while, until were explained
with examples.
Next followed the explanation of pipes and redirection
and how they can can be used to manipulate
input/output in scripts.
Raman concluded with a brief introduction on functions
and arguments usage in Bash.

The next session was conducted by Shiv Shankar on
MeshNet.
MeshNet is a community driven peer-to-peer network of
Wi-Fi nodes.
Shiv explained the concept and the requirements that
one needs to setup a MeshNet in ones locality.

The requirements are:
A low-level PC Pentium 200, 128 MB RAM ,USB and
CD-ROM. Rs.2000

A Wi-Fi Adapter preferably the Linksys WUSB-11 $40
approx Rs2000

Cabling and other Equipment Rs1000

The MESHAP Live CD Distro free :)

The setup is simple as one just inserts the Cd and the
connect is up.
Shiv mentioned the need for at least 2 Nodes to be
present within the range of the Wi-Fi adapter.
Typical range is around 1 Km Diameter and the range
can be increased with additional gain or transmitting
at a lower bit-rate(am i right? )

The project is in a nascent stage and will start
around March.

There was a call for Volunteers after the
introduction, which resulted in a series of questions.

A number of Factors were identified.
They include :
* The Community : The MeshNet is driven by the
community and an active community is required for the
development/growth of the MeshNet project.

*Technical Issues : Apart from the Wi-Fi Adapter and
the PC , a rooftop is available such that line of
sight is maintained for the ADHOC Network.

*LEGAL : Shiv assured the crowd that the MeshNet will
operate within the bandwidth that is termed legal by
the INdian Government.

*Commercial : Shiv explained a scenario where a
community can poll in their Internet Bandwidth so that
a "Grid" is formed and members of the MeshNEt can draw
"additional" bandwidth from the Net. In case their
connections are not used their bandwidth will be made
available to others. Again, a lot of issues surround
this as the Broadband Providers might not agree with
this service.

After the Brainstorming Session Raman mentioned about
the offer from RMK Engg College for a FLOSS Session at
their College Premises. Interested Volunteers can
contact Raman. The event will be held during the third
week of January.

The meeting was dispersed at around 1740 hrs.

Regards,
Toufeeq Hussain

PS: Sorry If I've misspelled any names.

From ramanraj at vsnl.com  Sat Dec 11 22:37:33 2004
From: ramanraj at vsnl.com (Ramanraj K)
Date: Sat Dec 11 22:37:25 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Meshnet - license issues
References: <20041211133729.24922.qmail@web12702.mail.yahoo.com>

  Toufeeq wrote:

>*LEGAL : Shiv assured the crowd that the MeshNet will
>operate within the bandwidth that is termed legal by
>the INdian Government.
>
As of now, "indoor" use of wireless within the 2.40-2.4835 MHz bandwidth 
is de-licensed, though the recent broadband policy is in favour of such 
freedom for outdoor use also.   Some background material:

A very effective representation was sent to TRAI by Siddarth, in July 
2004, requesting for a common free wireless space: 
http://www.trai.gov.in/spectrum/siddharth.pdf

The broadband policy announced is available at:

http://www.cable-quest.com/broadbandpolicy2004.htm

<quote>
(e) Terrestrial Wireless Recognising that terrestrial wireless is 
another upcoming technology platform for Broadband, it has been decided 
in principle to de-licence 2.40-2.48 GHz band for low-power outdoor use 
on non-protection, non-interference and non-exclusive basis. Necessary 
notification shall be issued. Further, notification regarding 
delicensing 2.40-2.4835 MHz band for low power indoor permitting use of 
all technologies, which inter-alia include those based on IEEE 802.11b 
and 802.11g standards, has been issued.
To accelerate penetration of Broadband and Internet, the 5.15-5.35 GHz 
band shall be de-licensed for the indoor use of low power Wi-Fi systems. 
For outdoor use, the band 5.25-5.35 GHz shall be de-licensed in 
consultation with DoS and delicensing in the band 5.15-5.25 GHz would be 
considered after the process of vacation. Alternative spectrum bands 
which are not in high usage and could be deployed for Broadband 
services, shall also be explored and identified.
</quote>

http://www.voicendata.com/content/vndtoday/104090301.asp
<quote>
However, the restriction about indoor/in-campus use continues. For 
outdoor hotspots in public areas, you still need a license from the WPC, 
with violations are still illegal and liable for a penalty.
</quote>

It is only a question of a time before which "outdoor" use would be 
delicensed,  in accordance with the Broadband Policy, 2004.  Please 
document the relevant notifications from WPC as you go forward on this. HTH.

-Ramanraj.

The command is:

If you don't do that, it'll complain. The remount option is essential.

In-Reply-To: <8816fcf804121004427bef7574@mail.gmail.com>

Hi all,

These are just my PERSONAL thoughts. Mail would be little big, but
I thought its high time to share it.
If you dont like this, you have all the right to send to /dev/null.
My intention is not to bring difference of opinion.

I have not given my contribution in any of the Linux fest or monthly
seminars. But I have been in the mailing list for the past 4 years
or more and I have attended few monthly meets and linux fests.

1.Better the Best
Linux is very good.But try to see and learn good things even if
is present in Opponent(MS). Be Open to the change.

2.Good wine needs no advertisement
I know linux is great for many people including me. But that does
not mean everybody should use that. If people or any persons finds
it good, Linux will have its own days. The usage of Linux should be
need based and not because it has got lot of featues and free.

3.Be ready to change and Be open.
I am ardent fan of linux, but if anything better I get I am ready
to change and I find nothing wrong in that if anybody is openminded
and understands clearly.

4.Share your knowledge
If you want to help people it does not necessarily mean it should
be only in the form of Linux. You can share your programming tricks,
tips and special or good ideas whatever it be.
Dont say you have GOOGLE for that. GOOGLE is not the only solution.
If ANYBODY can get ANYTHING using GOOGLE, there is NO POINT in we
getting technical Queries in our mailing lists.

I initially started this thread for making people share their knowledge
in tools related to Linux. Thereby I thought people will start realise
the benefits of using these tools and hence Linux environment.

I think Wikipaedia is doing good inspite of materials like that existed
before its arrival. Who knows, one day ILUGC's site may become top most
link in the tldp.org or linux.com or linux.org or kernel.org.

But I have seen people saying that this is reduntant because you have
everything on net. I strongly disagree to this, with reason being
when starting GOOGLE did not thought that they will be reduntatn(I
believe one or more search engines existed before GOOGLE). Similarly
Linus Torvalds knew Operating systems before he created one. In total
better the best OR products whatever it may be dig its own grave if a
better one comes.

So share your knowledge in whatever form and add some link anywhere in the
web so that people would contribute their knowledge(Though, I dont know
much, atleast I am ready to share whatever I know and whenever possible).

I value other peoples' time the most. Though I was not able to come
in flesh and Blood and help in any of the ILUGC activities,
I think, one does not need to help a person  or Community  only  by
coming in person. Also, I am sorry to say, but found from my experience
that inspite of repeated calling, I found people unwilling to come either
to monthly meet or Linux Fest(s). I dont know whether they dont find
anything interesting or they dont find time.

All the time I found only the same hardworking volunteers Barathi and
Raman along with few others.I should appreciate the efforts and spirit
with all of you inspite of my inability to do the same to your extents.

Please understand, my intention is not to hurt anybody's feelings,
but only to put forth my ideas and discuss for the reason that in ILUGC
mailing list, I think I can openly put forth my views.

Thanks for your spending your time reading this.

Thanks and regards
carti

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Mon Dec 13 14:40:48 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Mon Dec 13 15:10:02 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] NAT/Port forwarding on a DAX Router
In-Reply-To: <557E17BE74D22143B7BE70EB60E33E9913BE70D4@shlmsg01.ad.infosys.com>
Message-ID: <20041213091048.278BC329DA@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> 
> When I enter my IP in the browser it takes me to the web-based
> configuration login prompt of the router.
> 
> It should re-direct the request to my web server instead.
> 
  If by 'my IP' you mean your ISP-assigned dynamic IP address,
then this behaviour is correct for a NATed setup with a broadband
router. The ISP-facing interface of the router gets the
ISP-assigned IP address. If the router configuration page is
enabled on all its interfaces, then it will display that
configuration page when you type it into your browser, either
on the LAN or the WAN.

  If you want it to redirect http requests to the internal
LAN, you need to enable DNAT or port-forwarding. This is
possible with a Linux-embedded router (built with a Linux
Router Project image or a more recent derivative), but not
necessarily with all the commercial broadband routers that
are available. Some of them use Linux, but DNAT may not
be a configurable option on all models. DAX probably
uses Linux, but without DNAT support.

  If you want a fully-configurable NAT setup with DNAT,
check out routerlinux at http://www.routerlinux.com
It's a minimal-Linux distro based on uClibc and busybox,
and fits in 16 MB or less.

The only issue is that it supports only PPPoE and dialup
WAN interfaces. PPPoA on USB DSL modems, which is
commonly used by Chennai ISPs, is not supported, even if
the USB modem in question has support in the mainstream
kernel.

  If you think that this needs to change, then try to
patch the routerlinux kernel source with support for
the USB modem; test and validate it; and submit the
patch to routerlinux. The next release of
routerlinux can then be useful for more broadband
users here, and they need not pay for an overpriced
broadband router provided by their ISP :-).

(I already use routerlinux, but I have BSNL DIAS,
which uses PPPoE and is therefore fully supported).

-Siva

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Mon Dec 13 15:55:26 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Mon Dec 13 16:24:25 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] NAT/Port forwarding on a DAX Router
In-Reply-To: <557E17BE74D22143B7BE70EB60E33E9913D23AE1@shlmsg01.ad.infosys.com>
Message-ID: <20041213102526.6D855329DA@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> 
> How do I check for DNAT support in my router?
> 
  If it's not in the manual or the configuration page,
then it's probably not enabled. You can try poking
around using ssh (into the LAN-side interface of the
router), but there will most probably be a root
password set, and sshd may not be running on the
router. Try telnet as well.
> 
> My router uses PPPoA and its not a USB DSL Modem.
> It's an ethernet based router.
>
  There's nothing further that you can do with the
ISP-provided router, since it's mostly a black box. 
Internally, on the WAN side, it obviously interfaces to
the cable provided by the ISP. This is probably just
a stock DSL DMT or G.lite chipset that appears internal
to the router as a PPPoA interface (assuming it's
a Linux router). It then routes and NATs from that
interface to its LAN-facing Ethernet interface.

  With a routerlinux setup, it does exactly the same
thing, except that the routerlinux box is a 'white box'
or even a 'glass box', that replaces the 'black box'
provided by the ISP.  With routerlinux, you would need
to use the ISP-provided USB DSL modem instead of their
broadband router. The USB DSL modem would connect to
the routerlinux box (with the right driver stack, this
would then appear inside the routerlinux system as a
PPPoA interface). You can then do anything with the
PPPoA interface - at least anything that netfilter/iptables
supports, including DNAT.

  What's the advantage of this setup? The USB DSL modem
option is usually less expensive, and you have full
control over netfilter/iptables, so you have a fully
configurable firewall - with the right utilities,
you can do lots of useful things, including support
for multiple ISPs, bonding, fallback routing, load
balancing, multiple zoning (DMZs), etc.

 The downside is that
you need a minimal PC to run routerlinux - any old 486/
Pentium with 16 MB of RAM, a small hard disk and a
couple of ethernet NICs should be fine. For a more
robust embedded platform, look for a Soekris Engineering
Elan platform or a GCT/Allwell Eden platform - both
these are expensive (~$200-$300) alternatives.
 
-Siva

LEAF would be a better option IMHO www.leaf.sf.net. Far more powerful and
flexible. Can boot off a single floppy or dual floppy configuration. I've
used it extensively on VIA C3/Eden ITX form factor systems. Cost me $275. I
put LEAF on a CF and went chugging on.

Word of caution. Creating CF is not an easy task. I used a IDE-CF adaptor.
Hard to find here. Start with floppies. Easy but unreliable. For ease of
use, I'd recommend going with CD and isolinux. Doc for LEAF is fairly
detailed.

Mohan

On Mon, Dec 13, 2004 at 05:55:09PM +0530, S Mohan wrote:

>LEAF would be a better option IMHO www.leaf.sf.net. Far more powerful and
>flexible. Can boot off a single floppy or dual floppy configuration. I've
>used it extensively on VIA C3/Eden ITX form factor systems. Cost me $275. I

See if you can't telnet into that router (most el cheapo routers dont do
ssh but they do support telnet, or at least have a serial port that you can
plug into and talk to it using hyperterminal / minicom etc)

You may have to enable telnet in that web management interface - so then
you can enable port forwarding there, quite often though the web interface
doesnt support it

Quite a few of these PPPoA ADSL modems are based on generic chipsets like
Aztech / Buffalo etc.  So they should definitely support what you are
looking for ...

From trshash84 at gmail.com  Mon Dec 13 22:13:19 2004
From: trshash84 at gmail.com (T.R.Shashwath)
Date: Mon Dec 13 22:15:23 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] need help on soundcard configuration
In-Reply-To: <20041211162454.4837.qmail@web8407.mail.in.yahoo.com>
References: <20041211162454.4837.qmail@web8407.mail.in.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <200412132213.20095.trshash84@gmail.com>

First, check if you've got ALSA installed - as root run:

# alsactl -v

My output is:
alsactl version 0.9.2

If you know that you've got ALSA, next step is to find the driver module for 
the card: I'm not sure of it, so check in http://www.alsa-project.org/

Then, get that module, and insert it. The instructions are there on that site. 
Finally, test the sound by playing your favourite file! :)

From suraj at symonds.net  Mon Dec 13 09:28:06 2004
From: suraj at symonds.net (Suraj)
Date: Mon Dec 13 22:58:28 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] basic q's
In-Reply-To: <1102955456.31631.210688855@webmail.messagingengine.com>
References: <1102955456.31631.210688855@webmail.messagingengine.com>
Message-ID: <20041213172805.GA25785@symonds.net>

Mohammed Riyaz wrote: 
,----
| 1.Some  times the umount  does not  work with  the cdrom.  even umount
| /dev/cdrom -f gives a device busy signal, what do u do then??
`----

Of course, you  cannot! because you are sitting on a  branch of a tree
and trying to cut  that branch off! What you should do  is to see what
programs are  using the cdrom. It might  just be a shell  in which you
have 'cd'ed into /cdrom.

,----
| 2.Is it possible to find  the files that have changed (added/modified)
| , in the last xx minutes?? (basically it is like running updatedb with
| updatedb reporting  whenever it finds  a new files..or  something like
| that)
`----

man find (and look for -cmin, -mmin)

,----
| 3.How do find what version of gtk has been installed??
`----

Simply, if  you  are  running on a  standard packaged version  of Gtk,
then all you need  to do is use your package manager  (like rpm -qa or
dpkg -l and  grep the output). But if you compiled  Gtk by source, you
can    either   run    'strings'    on   the    library   file    (ex:
/usr/local/lib/libgtk-1.2.so.0)  or if  by chance  you also  happen to
have the README file installed as  part of the make install, you could
check the README.

,----
| 4.How do u  find where the rpm has extracted  it's contentes to??(i am
| not   talking  about   well  packed   rpm's  which   install   to  the
| standard/expected directories)
`----

AFAIK  rpm can be  converted to  a cpio  archive. But  my info  may be
dated. 

,----
| 5.Is  make distclean  equivalent to  uninstall?? what  about makefiles
| whcih dont provide this option?  how do u uninstall then??
`----

No! distclean  is similar  to 'make clean'  but slightly  different in
that it also deletes files  created by configure and friends. When you
run configure you might have  noticed that its slower during the first
run but faster during the successive runs (if you dont distclean, that
is). This is because configure 'caches' some of the info it found into
certain  files.    when  you  do  make  distclean,   this  cache  gets
cleared. (this  might be useful  when configuration changes  (like you
upgraded some dependant development library since last 'make')

However, If you want to uninstall, you should do 'make uninstall'.  Of
course, if your Makefile does not contain an 'uninstall' rule then you
are,  unfortunately,  on your  own :)    You can  either look   at the
Makefile and 'figure out' what gets installed (*VERY PAINFUL*, IMO) OR
have a neat wrapper around install ;) 

I  have this  bash function  as  a wrapper  to install  (install is  a
program that gets called by most sane Makefiles while 'Make'ing):

function install {
echo `date` $@ >>/usr/local/log/myinstall.log
`which install` $@
}


Watch out!  There  might be some badly written  Makefiles that may use
'cp' and such instead of 'install'.

Good luck!

  -Suraj

--

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Tue Dec 14 09:28:13 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Tue Dec 14 09:57:09 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] NAT/Port forwarding on a DAX Router
In-Reply-To: <0I8N00FFUUHZJD@mmp3.vsnl.net>
Message-ID: <20041214035813.E26C5329DB@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> 
> LEAF would be a better option IMHO www.leaf.sf.net. Far more powerful and
> flexible. Can boot off a single floppy or dual floppy configuration. I've
> used it extensively on VIA C3/Eden ITX form factor systems. Cost me $275. I
> put LEAF on a CF and went chugging on.
> 
  IMO, LEAF is far more difficult to configure and customize than
Routerlinux. Although the goals and approaches of these projects is
similar, and all eventually owe their origins to the LRP (Linux Router
Project), there has  been a significant divergence since then.

  LEAF is heavily forked, and mostly used 2.2 kernels, except for
a few recent forks using 2.4. It is typically a single-floppy distro,
so it's smaller - but it's far harder to configure, since everything
has to work before building the image.

  OTOH, Routerlinux is 2.4 + Busybox + uClibc based, and is
basically a small slackware-like distro. It also uses slackware's
package management tools, so you can add, upgrade and remove packages
from a running system. Lots of tools, including sshd, vi, etc., so
customizing a running system is easier. A partial list of packages
follows:

Busybox + uClibc (includes a lot of useful stuff, including vi and wget)
Slackware-like BSD-style init (very minimal and simple)
IPtables
Microcom
Pluto (FreeS/WAN)
PPP
PPTP, PPTPD
IProute2
Zebra (BGP-4, OSPF, RIP)
OpenSSL
OpenSSH
UDHCP
DNSMasq
RP-PPPoE
Net-snmp
Net-tools
Samba (optional, for NAS-type appliances)
rsync (optional, for automated backups for NAS-type appliances)

  Best of all, Routerlinux is a read-only root distro - only the
session-dependent temporaries go into ramdisk mounted at /var,
everything else is invariant. You can pull the plug on it and
nothing happens. Mine has been running for 14 months out of a
*hard disk* and I just turn the system on and off like an appliance
and nothing happens. It's a little-known and well-kept secret,
but hard disks are extremely reliable when used as read-only
media and kept always on, i.e. rotating. Just try not to spin
them down and up frequently - that really kills them quickly.
I have a Seagate 3120 (from 1990 or so) that's still going
strong, and it's now in a Routerlinux box.

> Word of caution. Creating CF is not an easy task. I used a IDE-CF adaptor.
> Hard to find here. Start with floppies. Easy but unreliable. For ease of
> use, I'd recommend going with CD and isolinux. Doc for LEAF is fairly
> detailed.

  Routerlinux can also be put into a CF, USB flash, Smartmedia or any
other bootable medium, and it will probably be even more reliable.
It's also trivial technically to put routerlinux on CF - it uses LILO,
so it's no different from putting it on a hard disk. I also have it
running from DiskonChip (a single-chip flash device) on a GCT/Allwell
STB 1030N (an all solid-state x86 PC in a set-top box form-factor). But
why bother? - used, small hardisks are available for peanuts and
work fine. Whole headless Pentium I/II machines without keyboard and
monitor are readily available for peanuts, even in Chennai, and are
perfectly suited for running RouterLinux. This is Rs.1000 (~$20) deal,
not a $300 deal, although you can pay that much if you want greater
reliability. If you want better reliability than Huawei/ZTE/Cisco, it
can be done, but at a small price premium.

  My own advice: Get a 430TX or VX board (with 16 MB SDRAM), any
Pentium classic CPU, and an oldie but goldie Seagate 40/80/120 MB (not GB!)
IDE hard disk. Get two PCI 10/100 NICs (I prefer tulips, but anything
will do, say Realteks). Temporarily connect a CDROM, monitor and
keyboard to perform the installation of routerlinux from CD.
Once it's installed, remove them and perform all further operations
using ssh over the network.

  I have another great (but untested) idea: run routerlinux in an
unprivileged domain using the Xen para-virtualization monitor, on
the same system as your main Linux desktop. This way, the additional
hardware costs are zero, and you'll only need about 1% of the CPU
cycles of any recent multi-GHz system.

-Siva
From vallinayagam at ureach.com  Mon Dec 13 23:30:19 2004
From: vallinayagam at ureach.com (V.K.Vallinayagam)
Date: Tue Dec 14 10:00:30 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] basic q's - alternative to "find"
Message-ID: <200412140430.XAA01204@www20.ureach.com>

Hi,
  If you are not a frequent user of "find"'s advanced options
and find it a pain to remember them or read the manual. ( Which
is the case with most gnu tools like "find"), there is an
alternate way which I use.
  Use TCL language , ie tclsh (tcl shell ). The fileutil package
has simpler find function and file functions. In this approach,
you may need to type few more words to accomplish but the
commands are more easier to keep in the head. This approach
suits people who are not frequent users and are not looking for
brevity, but looking for ease of remembering.
  
 The benefit of this language is - you have the syntactic
simplicity like command line but a very powerful language
beneath.Most unix commands have complex options because of the
limitations of the shell interpreter. 

Regards
V.K.Vallinayagam

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Mon Dec 13 23:55:05 2004
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Tue Dec 14 13:25:15 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Serial communication through user space!!
In-Reply-To: <1103006615.2446.17.camel@Morphis>
Message-ID: <20041214075505.64658.qmail@web50210.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi,

--- Raja Mallik <raja.mallik@moschip.com> wrote:
> How do I make my user program listen to serial port
> COM1, COM2?

Depends on whether you want to do blocking or
non-blocking I/O. If you want to do blocking, you can
use the read/write driver calls. 

ssize_t (*read) (struct file *, char *, size_t, loff_t
*);

ssize_t (*write) (struct file *, const char *, size_t,
loff_t *);

If you want to do non-blocking I/O, then you must use
poll and select.

unsigned int (*poll) (struct file *, struct
poll_table_struct *);

Please check this link:

Character Drivers:
http://www.xml.com/ldd/chapter/book/ch03.html

If you want to send/receive commands, you can use
ioctl:

int (*ioctl) (struct inode *, struct file *, unsigned
int, unsigned long);

Enhanced Char Driver Operations:
http://www.xml.com/ldd/chapter/book/ch05.html

You will use the corresponding read, write, ioctl
system calls in user-space.

Regards,

K Shakthi

K Shakthi
Specsoft (Hexaware Technologies), ASIC Design Center
http://www.geocities.com/shakthimaan

	jaharkes @ cs.cmu.edu in reply to RMS on linux.kernel
From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Tue Dec 14 06:44:54 2004
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Tue Dec 14 20:15:10 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] problem:with cli(), sti() 
In-Reply-To: <20041214111828.36864.qmail@web8403.mail.in.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20041214144455.37500.qmail@web50207.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi Madhukar,

--- Madhukar mythri <madhukar_linux@yahoo.co.in>
wrote:
> As i understood by reading the Bottom-half's
> concept's
> is :
> when cpu executing ISR... if interrupt come's then..
> it maintain's BH- queue's such that no loss of
> interrupt's..... is it???

The interrupt handling function that you register is
carried out with interrupts disabled. So, you must do
very little tasks here and exit, as the interrupts on
the system are disabled during the time. So, you would
do only what is required and leave the rest to
BHs/tasklets. 

Rest could mean awakening processes, I/O operation
etc. Remember that during BHs/tasklets interrupts are
enabled and hence your code should be re-entrant. Also
in BHs/tasklets you _shouldn't_:
- sleep
- access user-space
- call schedule()

> if we just put "mark_bh(IMMEDIATE_BH);"
> at end of ISR execution is sufficent i hope??? is
> it??

Why don't you check the example (short/short.c) here:
http://examples.oreilly.com/linuxdrive2/

There are also ample code examples in driver/ in the
kernel source directory which you can browse, study
and learn. 

Regards,

K Shakthi

K Shakthi
Specsoft (Hexaware Technologies), ASIC Design Center
http://www.geocities.com/shakthimaan

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Wed Dec 15 10:05:40 2004
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi S)
Date: Wed Dec 15 10:10:58 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Fwd: Call for papers Fosdem 2005 (26, 27 Feb @ Brussels)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0412151000250.1132-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>


At the start of next year FOSDEM, the most important Belgian Free
Software event will be back again. As on the previous occasions there
will also be an embedded track, for which we are looking for speakers.  
All the necessary info can be found in the following call for papers.  
Feel free to distribute, and tell other people about it.
 
3th EMBEDDED SYSTEMS and OPERATING SYSTEMS track at FOSDEM 2005 
=============================================================== 
  
26 - 27 February 2005, Brussels 
 
Call for papers 
---------------- 
 
The 2005 edition of FOSDEM (Free and Open Source Developers' European
Meeting; http://www.fosdem.org) will take place in Brussels, Belgium
on 26 and 27 February 2005. For the third time, a track on Embedded
Systems and Operating Systems will be organized. The second edition
was quite succesful and attracted up to 150 attendants for certain
topics.
 
For last year's program see:  
http://www.embedded-kernel-track.org/2004/papers.html 
 
The use of Free Software in the infrastructure of embedded systems is
booming, e.g. by the use of Linux, uClinux, eCos, RedBoot, RTEMS and
many other Free Software components. More companies are supporting
embedded Free Software each day because of the reliability and cheap
licensing.
 
Operating system development has always been a very important topic in
Free Software.  As embedded and real-time systems typically have
special OS requirements, we organise this Free Embedded and OS
development track at FOSDEM.
 
This track provides a remarkable opportunity to present and discuss
the ongoing work in these areas, and we invite developers to present
their current projects. Technical topics of the conference include but
are not limited to :
 
* OS Development : kernel architecture and implementation, libraries 
  (e.g. Linux, BSD, uClinux, uClibc, newlib, ...) 
 
* Practical experiences in implementing Free Software in embedded
  systems (e.g. reverse engineering, porting  to (and adapting of) 
  commercial devices  (IPAQ, Linksys WRT54G,...), ...) 
 
* Toolchain and build environment  
  (e.g. crosstool, emdebian, openembedded, PTX dist, packaging, 
   scratchbox, Eclipse, Valgrind,...) 
 
* GUIs for embedded systems 
  (Gtk, Qt-(embedded), GPE, Qtopia, UI design with touchscreen, kdrive ...) 
 
* Multimedia applications for embedded systems 
  (e.g. integer-only decoders, Opieplayer, ... ) 
 
* Real-time extensions, nanokernels and hardware virtualization software 
  (e.g. RTAI, Adeos, KURT, L4, Qemu, User Mode Linux, ...) 
  
* Hard real-time OS's 
  (eCos, RTEMS, ...) 
 
* Open hardware and softcores 
  (e.g opencores.org, OpenRISC, LEON SPARC, FPGA's, specific design 
   restrictions for free systems...) 
 
* Safety and security certifications applied to Free software 
  (e.g. security measures in Embedded systems, SSL libraries, ...) 
 
* Free software licenses and embedded systems 
 
Authors are requested to submit their abstracts online to
embedded@fosdem.org before 3 January 2005. Notification of receipt
will be sent within 48 hours. Authors wishing to submit a full paper
(between 6 and 12 A4 pages), can do so in PS or PDF format.
 
The program committee will evaluate the abstracts and consists of: 
 
* Herman Bruyninckx, Professor at K.U.Leuven, Belgium 
* Geert Uytterhoeven, Sony NSCE, Belgium 
* Karim Yaghmour, Opersys, Canada 
* Peter De Schrijver (P2), Mind, Belgium 
* Russell King (RMK), ARM Linux Kernel Engineer, Deep Blue Solutions Ltd 
   
| Please do not send documents in a closed format. (*.doc,*.xls,*.ppt)     
| Use the open alternatives. (*.pdf,*.ps,*.html,*.txt)     
| Why? http://pallieter.is-a-geek.org:7832/~johan/word/english/     

See you at Fosdem, 
Philippe 

--
Bharathi S
