> 
> Welcome to this year's 49th issue of DWN, the weekly 
> newsletter for the Debian community. Bruce Byfield released a 
> short [1]introduction into apt-get on [2]NewsForge. Again, 
> developers were [3]advised to close bugs automatically with a 
> changelog entry only in connection with a proper description. 
> Jason Boxman wrote a [4]guideline for using Exim 4 and 
> Courier IMAP on a Debian system.
> 
>  1. http://www.newsforge.com/article.pl?sid=04/12/02/1710208
>  2. http://www.newsforge.com/
>  3. http://lists.debian.org/debian-devel/2004/12/msg00907.html
>  4. http://trekweb.com/~jasonb/articles/exim4_courier/
> 
> Constructive Critique of Debian. In a guest [5]editorial on 
> [6]DesktopLinux Binh Nguyen noted some key design attributes 
> of Debian that make it one of the strongest and most 
> versatile GNU/Linux distributions. He also observed certain 
> weaknesses and argued that a few simple improvements and a 
> more welcoming attitude to new users would significantly 
> improve Debian. He concluded that Debian is a competent and 
> robust distribution, but with a few critical flaws that have 
> led perception of it being an elitist distribution.
> 
>  5. http://www.desktoplinux.com/articles/AT7588639943.html
>  6. http://www.desktoplinux.com/
> 
> Geek Feminists in Debian. Bruce Byfield [7]reported about the 
> [8]Debian women sub-project and its beginnings. One of Debian 
> women's main roles is to help women become Debian developers, 
> partly by being supportive and encouraging, but also by 
> demystifying the process. Debian women has created a friendly 
> place for learning more about Debian and has drawn out many 
> women to talk about their experiences and ambitions.
> 
>  7. http://www.newsforge.com/article.pl?sid=04/12/03/173216
>  8. http://women.alioth.debian.org/
> 
> Multi-Head Computing.[9]OPENSense Solutions [10]announced the 
> availability of Groovix, a Debian-based multi-user computer. 
> Up to three sets of monitor, keyboard, mouse and speaker are 
> attached to a single AMD Athlon based computer. The 
> [11]system consists of Debian GNU/Linux with KDE as desktop 
> environment. The vendor stresses that they can't support 
> other configurations, but, apt-get install gnome is not that 
> hard to type.
> 
>  9. http://www.opensensesolutions.com/products.html
>  10. http://www.emediawire.com/releases/2004/12/emw187925.htm
>  11. http://opensensesolutions.com/software.html
> 
> Advertising on the Debian Website. Martin Michlmayr 
> [12]forwarded an inquiry to place advertising on the Debian 
> website. Stephen Frost would [13]welcome the potential 
> revenue stream. However, [14]several [15]developers 
> [16]didn't [17]like the idea and Alexander Schmehl even 
> [18]gave an example for content-driven advertising: if you 
> search for the terms "Debian" and "Linux", you'll get an 
> advertisement telling you the "true facts" about open source.
> 
>  12. http://lists.debian.org/debian-project/2004/12/msg00028.html
>  13. http://lists.debian.org/debian-project/2004/12/msg00039.html
>  14. http://lists.debian.org/debian-project/2004/12/msg00034.html
>  15. http://lists.debian.org/debian-project/2004/12/msg00046.html
>  16. http://lists.debian.org/debian-project/2004/12/msg00053.html
>  17. http://lists.debian.org/debian-project/2004/12/msg00068.html
>  18. http://lists.debian.org/debian-project/2004/12/msg00072.html
> 
> Support for SVG Icons. Jay Treacy [19]wondered how [20]SVG 
> (Scalable Vector Graphics) icons are supposed to be handled 
> in the Debian system. Josselin Mouette [21]explained that all 
> of GTK+ already supports them and where they are usually put 
> on the filesystem. Bill Allombert [22]added that the menu 
> manual only talks about XPM icons.
> 
>  19. http://lists.debian.org/debian-devel/2004/12/msg00869.html
>  20. http://www.w3.org/TR/SVG/
>  21. http://lists.debian.org/debian-devel/2004/12/msg00886.html
>  22. http://lists.debian.org/debian-devel/2004/12/msg00910.html
> 
> Ongoing dpkg Development. In a reply to an [23]intent to 
> package by Martin F. Krafft, Adam Heath [24]revealed future 
> plans for the dpkg-deb utility. In such a modular design 
> editing Debian package without the need to install them would 
> become an easy task. It would also support [25]excluding 
> entire directory hierarchies, such as /usr/share/doc.
> 
>  23. http://lists.debian.org/debian-devel/2004/12/msg00842.html
>  24. http://lists.debian.org/debian-devel/2004/12/msg01099.html
>  25. http://lists.debian.org/debian-devel/2004/12/msg01247.html
> 
> GNU/Linux Core Consortium. Bruce Perens [26]explained that 
> the GNU/Linux Core Consortium (LCC) is what he originally 
> proposed to do as the [27]LSB and would like to have Debian's 
> involvement. The main technical effect that he sees would be 
> that the names of some dynamic libraries would change, which 
> was [28]not [29]appreciated. The LCC [30]aims to complement 
> the LSB by agreeing on a single solutions for grey cases in the LSB.
> 
>  26. http://lists.debian.org/debian-devel/2004/12/msg00912.html
>  27. http://www.linuxbase.org/
>  28. http://lists.debian.org/debian-devel/2004/12/msg00915.html
>  29. http://lists.debian.org/debian-devel/2004/12/msg00940.html
>  30. http://lists.debian.org/debian-devel/2004/12/msg00975.html
> 
> GNOME Transition into Sarge finished. Jordi Mallach 
> [31]reported that [32]gconf-editor was the last component of 
> GNOME 2.8 that was pending to enter testing, which is done 
> already. Earlier he [33]reported that this has been the 
> smoothest transition to testing since GNOME 2.0. 
> Additionally, a new version of Evolution with all 
> release-critical bugs fixed has been uploaded.
> 
>  31. 
> http://oskuro.net/blog/freesoftware/gnome-2.8-sarge-2004-12-13-15-07
>  32. http://packages.debian.org/gconf-editor
>  33. 
> http://oskuro.net/blog/freesoftware/gnome-2.8-sarge-2004-12-03-18-19
> 
> Supporting Free Java. Arnaud Vandyck [34]asked other Java 
> developer to test their programs with a free runtime and 
> report the results. He started a [35]page where he will 
> document results of running projects with a free Java virtual 
> machine. His own [36]remarks contain experiences with a 
> project that makes heavy use of threads.
> 
>  34. http://www.livejournal.com/users/avdyk/9097.html
>  35. http://java.debian.net/index.php/DebianSupportsFreeJava
>  36. http://people.debian.org/~avdyk/freejava/

From zulfilee at midascomm.com  Wed Dec 15 15:56:23 2004
From: zulfilee at midascomm.com (zulfilee)
Date: Wed Dec 15 15:36:37 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Help required....Require a script to filter information
	from vmstat output...Clarification INside...
In-Reply-To: <97a0151404121501274a87ab04@mail.gmail.com>
References: <97a0151404121501274a87ab04@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <200412151556.24206.zulfilee@midascomm.com>

My vmstat shows

 procs                      memory      swap          io     system      cpu
 r  b  w   swpd   free   buff  cache   si   so    bi    bo   in    cs us sy id
 1  0  0  83256   3356   3240  41552    4   20    62    32  140   601  3  1 97

Here i get the fields using

$PROCS=`vmstat | sed -n   2,10p | tr -s " " | cut -d " " -f 1-4`
$MEMORY=`vmstat | sed -n   2,10p | tr -s " " | cut -d " " -f 5-7`

And so on

The sed is to strip the first line
Tr is to squeeze the spaces and cut to get the fileds I want

So you can just call echo $PROCS, $MEMORY, etc..
It can be made a lot easier if sed is used

Cheers
Z

From ramanraj at vsnl.com  Wed Dec 15 17:06:17 2004
From: ramanraj at vsnl.com (Ramanraj K)
Date: Wed Dec 15 17:06:29 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] GET/POST using XMLHttpRequest Object
References: <4173F252.5060406@md4.vsnl.net.in>
Message-ID: <41C021B1.7020704@vsnl.com>



> Is there a way to do a partial post or get in web forms?

Could be done using the XMLHttpRequest Object.
http://www.xulplanet.com/references/objref/XMLHttpRequest.html

example:
<script type="text/javascript">
  pg = new XMLHttpRequest();
  pg.open("GET", "test.php",false);
  pg.send(null);
  alert (pg.responseText);
</script>

Google's Suggest makes use of XMLHttpRequest object: 
http://www.google.com/ac.js
Mozilla Tinderbox-SeaMonkey uses it to update info.

Balachander, thanks for pointing to the Google Suggest page.

From sathya at Ultime.org  Wed Dec 15 05:09:03 2004
From: sathya at Ultime.org (sathya)
Date: Wed Dec 15 17:55:12 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Kernel source in FC3
Message-ID: <200412150509.04518.sathya@ultime.org>

FYI, RedHat has not provided the kernel source during the installation phase 
of FC-3. If you want to install it, the following ways are recommended from 
the README file :

In order to eliminate the redundancy inherent in providing a separate package 
for the kernel source code when that source code already exists in the 
kernel's .src.rpm file, Fedora Core 3 no longer includes the kernel-source 
package. Users that require access to the kernel sources can find them in the 
kernel .src.rpm file. To create an exploded source tree from this file, 
perform the following steps (note that <version> refers to the version 
specification for your currently-running kernel):

Obtain the kernel-<version>.src.rpm file from one of the following sources:

The SRPMS directory on the appropriate "SRPMS" CD iso image

The FTP site where you got the kernel package

By running the following command:

up2date --get-source kernel

Install kernel-<version>.src.rpm (given the default RPM configuration, the 
files this package contains will be written to /usr/src/redhat/)

Change directory to /usr/src/redhat/SPECS/, and issue the following command:

rpmbuild -bp --target=<arch> kernel.spec

(Where <arch> is the desired target architecture.)

On a default RPM configuration, the kernel tree will be 
locatedin /usr/src/redhat/BUILD/.

In resulting tree, the configurations for the specific kernels shipped in 
Fedora Core 3 are in the /configs/ directory. For example, the i686 SMP 
configuration file is named /configs/kernel-<version>-i686-smp.config. Issue 
the following command to place the desired configuration file in the proper 
place for building:

cp <desired-file> ./.config

Issue the following command:

make oldconfig

You can then proceed as usual.

You can get details about this if you open konqueror... which opens the FC3 
Release Notes... where all this is clearly specified.. also don't forget to 
install the "udev" update...

From fred at bytesforall.org  Wed Dec 15 17:51:56 2004
From: fred at bytesforall.org (Frederick Noronha (FN))
Date: Wed Dec 15 18:06:02 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] IOSN.net ... FLOSS primers, localisation toolket,
	project workspace
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.60.0412151751400.784@news.goa.bytesforall.org>

>From IOSN.net

The IOSN is producing a series of primers on Free/Open Source Software
(FOSS). The primers serve as introductory documents to FOSS in general, as
well as covering particular topic areas in greater detail. Their purpose is
to raise FOSS awareness, particularly among policy-makers, practitioners and
educators.

* FOSS General Introduction Primer * FOSS in Education Primer * FOSS Government 
and Policy Primer * FOSS Licensing Primer

Draft for public review and feedback.


Localization Toolkit

IOSN is in the process of developing localization toolkits that will aid
localization of FOSS software.

Project workspace

For localization projects that require an online presence and workspace,
contact us so that you can host and manage your project on IOSN. If you
already have a project, let us know so that localization projects in
different countries can collaborate on localization efforts.

* Localization resources

Resources

Training Materials

IOSN also produces free training materials for Free/Open Software.  Training
materials for end users are currently in development.

* User Guide to Using the Linux Desktop

This user guide is meant as an introductory guide for a user to use a modern
personal computer (PC) running the Linux operating system.  The main aim is
to provide a self-learning guide on how to use a modern Linux desktop
system. It assumes that the user has no prior knowledge of Linux or PC
usage.

* Other Linux and Free/Open Source  Software training resources

iosn-general Mailing List

The goals of the mailing list is to help foster more regional communication
and co-operation. Especially to provide a channel in which users from
countries where FOSS is relatively unknown can get help from the
international FOSS community, as well as help each other.

If you would still like to be part of this community, you can subscribe via
the link given below.

> page,disk,faults,cpu) in the output of the vmstat command.

Here's the output of vmstat on my machine:

procs -----------memory---------- ---swap-- -----io---- --system-- ----cpu----
 r  b   swpd   free   buff  cache   si   so    bi    bo   in    cs us sy id wa
 0  0      0  47068  38504  81028    0    0   129     7 1041    88  1  0 99  1

Assuming the output as above, the following (2 minute dirty hack) script that should do the job:

----8<------------8<-----------
#!/bin/sh
[ $1 -a $1 == "proc"   ] && vmstat | tail -2 | awk '{ print $1 "\t" $2 }' && exit
[ $1 -a $1 == "memory" ] && vmstat | tail -2 | awk '{ print $3 "\t" $4 "\t" $5 "\t" $6 }' && exit
[ $1 -a $1 == "swap"   ] && vmstat | tail -2 | awk '{ print $7 "\t" $8 }' && exit
[ $1 -a $1 == "io"     ] && vmstat | tail -2 | awk '{ print $9 "\t" $10 }' && exit
[ $1 -a $1 == "system" ] && vmstat | tail -2 | awk '{ print $11 "\t" $12 }' && exit
[ $1 -a $1 == "cpu"    ] && vmstat | tail -2 | awk '{ print $13 "\t" $14 "\t" $15 "\t" $16 "\t" $17 }' && exit
echo "usage: $0 { proc | memory | swap | io | system | cpu }"
----8<-----------8<------------

You might have to modify the awk chunk to suit your vmstat's output.
Want me to explain the code ? Buy me a drink ;-)

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.
http://www.chandrashekar.info/

From vallinayagam at ureach.com  Thu Dec 16 01:27:59 2004
From: vallinayagam at ureach.com (V.K.Vallinayagam)

Subject: [Ilugc] Help required....Require a script to filter information
	from vmstat output...Clarification INside...
Message-ID: <200412160627.BAA21899@www22.ureach.com>

Hi,
 The default command line tools may not be very convenient for
elaborate and sophisticated or customized monitoring.
 The following tools may be very convenient.It is summarised in
the following article.

 http://www.linuxjournal.com/node/7620/print

 The tools used are 
* libstatgrab  library
 http://www.i-scream.org/libstatgrab/
* ssclient based on this library (system statistics client)
 http://ssclient.sourceforge.net/

 You can create TCL commands that wrap the C functions of the
library using swig tool easily. Thereby u get commandline tools
like interface and feel.

Regards
V.K.Vallinayagam

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Wed Dec 15 23:38:53 2004
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)

Subject: [Ilugc] [OT] GNU/Linux Vidyashram
Message-ID: <20041216073853.37551.qmail@web50210.mail.yahoo.com>

Greetings!

This is a proposal to form the GNU/Linux Educational
Society, or call it, "GNU/Linux Vidyashram".

The aim is to organize/provide free lectures (atleast
once a fortnight, with lectures repeated if needed).
Due to rapid developments in GNU/Linux it is essential
that we meet often and share/discuss our knowledge.
Saturday/Sunday afternoon is good. We can start
different lecture series for different time periods
like, 2-weeks, 1-month, 2-months etc.

Leaving commercial training institutes apart (which
are more industry-oriented, like system and network
administration), the objective of GNU/Linux Vidyashram
is to constantly provide free-training to GNU/Linux
enthusiasts. I believe the commerical institutes don't
teach kernel programming, application development etc.
The free-teaching can also be useful for students who
are interested in doing projects.

I am on the lookout for lecture halls/institutions who
can provide the facilites at a minimal cost (for free
would be great!). Having a projector will help as one
can see and learn from the observation, rather than
deal with monotonous classroom-board teaching. I
remember, some of the IIT-M Electrical Engineering
Deparment students asking for some sessions like
these. Maybe we can organize the same with them? The
lectures _must_ be open to the public though.

I would like to initiate the above under ilugc-GNU
projects. We need to first cover shell scripting
before we can go into kernel programming. I would like
to volunteer for:

- BASH shell scripting
- KDevelop/Qt designer
- device driver programming
- Linux assembly

Similarily, if more people are interested we can start
sessions for perl/python/gtk/qt/c++/java/php/ etc. on
GNU/Linux etc.

Your thoughts?

Regards,

K Shakthi

Ramaprasanna wrote: 
,----
| Can a Linux router Operating system  be installed in Routers? Or it is
| meant for PC based routers?
`----

There are several 'PC-like' routers (they are definitely not PC in the
literal sense). But they also have a  memory, a way to "boot" an OS, a
network interface (duh!) and <drum rolls please...> a CPU!

Check out:

http://www.linuxdevices.com/articles/AT6449817972.html

and in general, http://www.linuxdevices.com/

Hi,
 I like the idea. But here is my alternate thought. 
This idea, ilugc meet, all seems to be more  altruistic in tone,
enabling people to learn linux.People volunteering for no
financial benefits but for the joy of being involved in linux. I
think Linux needs more capitalisitic kind of approach to become
popular. 
 That is, you should help others to earn money using linux. This
is my view - Charity is not a self-sustaining activity. All
charity activities are indirectly or directly funded by
business. Business ( profit based ) is self-sustaining.
Therefore Business is equally noble as charity .

 Lectures can be on following topic.Say initially the lectures
may be free, later can make it chargeable or make premium
lectures chargeable. 

 Some commercial applications of linux can be as follows.
 
1.Enable DTP houses to move to Linux.
  1.1 How to design visiting cards, brochures using linux and
related tools.
  1.2 How to design business letters, project reports. using
linux tools.

2.Enable digital photo studios and Video studios to use Linux
for their editing composing and other manipulations.( Like those
they use for marriage videos.)

  Advantage for user.

1. These setups can use non-pirated software. No legal problems.
2. Save on money from buying commercial softwares. Most
opens-source stuffs are free.
3. Stability of platform.
4. No vendor dependency for upgrades etc.

 I personally know one digital studio, which  supposed to give
my photo in 10 minutes, took 50 minutes because the windows PC
was crashing as these photo manipulations use lot of memory. I
had to wait for one hour unnecessarily.When I enquired they said
 it(PC problem ) does happen often.

 I personally use sodipodi for my Business card design . I know
nearly everyone uses coreldraw or adobe and of that nearly 90%
market uses pirated stuffs.
  Create wealth using OSS and also help others create wealth
using OSS. This way OSS will become popular. OSS - Open Source
Software.

Regards
V.K.Vallinayagam

wrote:

> Greetings!
> 
> This is a proposal to form the GNU/Linux Educational
> Society, or call it, "GNU/Linux Vidyashram".
> 
> The aim is to organize/provide free lectures (atleast
> once a fortnight, with lectures repeated if needed).
> Due to rapid developments in GNU/Linux it is essential
> that we meet often and share/discuss our knowledge.
> Saturday/Sunday afternoon is good. We can start
> different lecture series for different time periods
> like, 2-weeks, 1-month, 2-months etc.
> 
> Leaving commercial training institutes apart (which
> are more industry-oriented, like system and network
> administration), the objective of GNU/Linux Vidyashram
> is to constantly provide free-training to GNU/Linux
> enthusiasts. I believe the commerical institutes don't
> teach kernel programming, application development etc.
> The free-teaching can also be useful for students who
> are interested in doing projects.
> 
> I am on the lookout for lecture halls/institutions who
> can provide the facilites at a minimal cost (for free
> would be great!). Having a projector will help as one
> can see and learn from the observation, rather than
> deal with monotonous classroom-board teaching. I
> remember, some of the IIT-M Electrical Engineering
> Deparment students asking for some sessions like
> these. Maybe we can organize the same with them? The
> lectures _must_ be open to the public though.
> 
> I would like to initiate the above under ilugc-GNU
> projects. We need to first cover shell scripting
> before we can go into kernel programming. I would like
> to volunteer for:
> 
> - BASH shell scripting
> - KDevelop/Qt designer
> - device driver programming
> - Linux assembly
> 
> Similarily, if more people are interested we can start
> sessions for perl/python/gtk/qt/c++/java/php/ etc. on
> GNU/Linux etc.
> 
> Your thoughts?

Arjun Baskaran wrote: 
,----
| i have  all the fedoro core  images how to install  from these images?
| no cdrom drive
`----

Interesting... 

DISCLAIMER: Random idea. MAY or MAY NOT work.

Create a  partition that is as  big as your  ISO image and then  do dd
if=fedora.iso  of=/dev/hdaXXX and  try to  boot off  it using  grub. I
doubt if this would work.

Alternatively, if you have a network card and another machine, setup a
bootp server that sends this ISO and boot from your network card. Huge
volumes of machines are installed this way in my organisation.

cheers,

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Fri Dec 17 06:20:09 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Fri Dec 17 06:49:12 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] can linux router OS can be installed in Routers?
Message-ID: <20041217005009.74192329DD@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>


> Can a Linux router Operating system be installed in Routers? Or it is meant
> for PC based routers?
> 
  Many commercial routers (e.g. Linksys) actually use an LRP (Linux
Router Project) derivative internally. So, yes, a Linux router-centric
distro can and is installed in many routers.

  Juniper uses a BSD-derived OS called Junos on most of its routers.

  Cisco uses Linux in various midrange products, including PIX
firewalls and IDS intrusion-detection system, as well as various
system-supervisory boxes. Most of these are just stock 1U x86
boxes running Linux from a flash disk, with a userland consisting
of both open-source and Cisco-proprietary software. 

  However, this doesn't imply that you can go out and buy a Cisco
CSR-1 and convert it into a Beowulf cluster :-)

-Siva

Arjun Baskaran wrote:
,----
| i have  all the fedoro core  images how to install  from these images?
| no cdrom drive
`----

Interesting...

DISCLAIMER: Random idea. MAY or MAY NOT work.

Create a  partition that is as  big as your  ISO image and then  do dd
if=fedora.iso  of=/dev/hdaXXX and  try to  boot off  it using  grub. I
doubt if this would work.

Alternatively, if you have a network card and another machine, setup a
bootp server that sends this ISO and boot from your network card. Huge
volumes of machines are installed this way in my organisation.

cheers,

Message: 12
Date: Fri, 17 Dec 2004 06:20:09 +0530 (IST)
From: Sivasankar Chander <siva@dias.ath.cx>
Subject: Re: [Ilugc] can linux router OS can be installed in Routers?
To: ilugc@ae.iitm.ac.in
Cc: Sivasankar Chander <siva@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>
Message-ID: <20041217005009.74192329DD@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>
Content-Type: text/plain; charset=US-ASCII


> Can a Linux router Operating system be installed in Routers? Or it is
meant
> for PC based routers?
>
  Many commercial routers (e.g. Linksys) actually use an LRP (Linux
Router Project) derivative internally. So, yes, a Linux router-centric
distro can and is installed in many routers.

  Juniper uses a BSD-derived OS called Junos on most of its routers.

  Cisco uses Linux in various midrange products, including PIX
firewalls and IDS intrusion-detection system, as well as various
system-supervisory boxes. Most of these are just stock 1U x86
boxes running Linux from a flash disk, with a userland consisting
of both open-source and Cisco-proprietary software.

  However, this doesn't imply that you can go out and buy a Cisco
CSR-1 and convert it into a Beowulf cluster :-)

-Siva

From vijairaj_sr at rediffmail.com  Fri Dec 17 04:10:22 2004
From: vijairaj_sr at rediffmail.com (Vijairaj  R)
Date: Fri Dec 17 09:40:24 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] how to install from iso images
Message-ID: <20041217041104.23014.qmail@webmail45.rediffmail.com>

I once successfully installed FreeBSD from an iso immage while running the installation from a linux box. I used the qemu (PC emulator) like this.(you should be a root)

$qemu -hda /dev/sda -cdrom /path/to/iso -boot d -nics 0

Also, qemu is a very useful tool for testing newly compiled kernels.

..WARNING..WARNING.. Go through the documentation before you try, this is potentially risky and you can end up bith a blanked disk.

regards
 Vijairaj

id using an email client, use yahoopops which

interface. it used to work perfectly till last yahoo
upgrade (when they gave us 100 mb) but now it wont
delete mails from server so u need to visit your yahoo
inbox manually once in a while & manually delete the
mails but works sweetly for receiving & sending
mails!!! download from

--- Madhukar mythri <madhukar_linux@yahoo.co.in>
wrote:
> I have Good skill's in:
>  C/C++
>  Kernel-internal's
>  Device driver's(serial & PCI)
>  Networking programming & concept's
>  RTOS concept's.

Thanks.

Yes, I would like to start of soon with kernel
programming (Madhukar, myself, and other volunteers).
But, we must first make sure that we teach shell
scripting first, as programmers must be comfortable
working with the shell (will need to understand use of
Makefile, insmod, rmmod, user interaction scripting
etc.).

Once we finish shell scripting we can start of kernel
programming, assembly. In January, we can also
parallely start application programming (Perl
-Toufeeq). Teaching will have to more applied, rather
than text-book oriented. So, we must teach by giving
examples on how to solve the problem, rather than
explain syntax usage or what is already there in the
book, and in the man pages. Maybe, you can also start
training sessions in your locality :)

The main objective of GNU/Linux Vidyashram is to
educate/teach people. We should also expand our
operations in conducting seminars/workshops at
educational institutions (schools/colleges). 

Sorry for the wrong dates. The schedule will be on
weekends only. Depending on availability of the
venues, we shall inform you the dates, well in
advance.

Thanks again,

K Shakthi

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Fri Dec 17 19:08:42 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Fri Dec 17 19:37:40 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] {Query}{Marketing} Large Linux storage array
In-Reply-To: <20041217033433.69002.qmail@web52510.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20041217133842.1A021329DD@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> Is there a market in India for 1TB to 6TB external
> sata storage appliance attahment to Linux servers ?
> What Raid levels it must support ?
> How inexpensive it should be for entry level ?
> 
  Not really the answer to your query, but AMI
(American Megatrends) makes a 1U x86 embedded Linux
NAS appliance that supports 4 hot-swap SCSI drives
and connects via gigabit ethernet. This is available
in India for ~$4000 (~Rs. 1.75 lakhs) without
SCSI drives (probably not what can be called
entry level).

  I'm not sure about its innards, but it's probably
a Samba box that connects to mainly Windows networks
(perhaps with an NFS option also).

-Siva
From siva at dias.ath.cx  Fri Dec 17 19:13:03 2004

Subject: [Ilugc] how to install from iso images
In-Reply-To: <20041217041104.23014.qmail@webmail45.rediffmail.com>
Message-ID: <20041217134303.4355C329DD@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> I used the qemu (PC emulator) like this.(you should be a root)
>
>$qemu -hda /dev/sda -cdrom /path/to/iso -boot d -nics 0
>
  Brilliant! Obvious in retrospect, but certainly the most
unorthodox use of emulators (like qemu) that I've ever
encountered.

-Siva

Hi

First, can you tell us what distro you're using? It's hard to make out what's 
happening, if we don't know that. :-)

Now, it looks, from what I see, like all the config files are missing. I don't 
know much about what should be done, but you might try rebuilding them by 
hand (very hard), reinstalling from the binary package, or downloading the 
source from http://www.mplayerhq.com and compiling it. If you tell us what 
distro you're using, we might be able to figure out more.

BTW, I notice that you're running as root - be advised that this can be VERY 
dangerous. I'd recommend that you set up another user with restricted 
priviledges, and use root only for system admin tasks, and log out as soon as 
those tasks are done.

Shash

Not necessary.
It looks for user-specific config files in the home
directory.
If it fails it falls back to hardcoded
configuration(default). This tries to launch a plain
vanilla mplayer.

> 
> On Friday 17 Dec 2004 6:50 am, Ashok Antony wrote:
> > Hi All,
> >  I have installed mplayer in my sytem.
> >
> > then I typed the follwing command at that time it
> > throws the following error. I have attached the
> error
> > it throws.

Before this, did you go through the README file for
enabling codecs and stuff?

and... did you do ./configure --enable-gui , this will
install gmplayer, the gui frontend.

Second, try to get the codecs installed. This is
causing the problem.You'r trying to play a 'wmv' file,
a codec that's not installed by default in Linux.

Look below.

> > Requested audio codec family [acelp] (afm=dshow)
> not
> > available.
> > Enable it at compilation.
> > Cannot find codec for audio format 0x130.

Now try a "simple" video file mpg or ogg.

> > It seems there is no Xvideo support for your video
> > card available.
> > Run 'xvinfo' to verify its Xv support and read
> > DOCS/HTML/en/devices.html#xv!
> > See 'mplayer -vo help' for other (non-xv) video
> out
> > drivers. Try -vo x11

Try Xv as the video driver.
This seemed to work for me.
set -vo=Xv during startup of mplayer.(chk README)

> > Requested video codec family [mss1] (vfm=dshow)
> not
> > available.
> > Enable it at compilation.
> > Cannot find codec matching selected -vo and video
> > format 0x3153534D.

Again some codecs seem to be missing. This time for
video.Is X started when your playing this ?

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Sat Dec 18 08:51:05 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Sat Dec 18 09:20:14 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Fwd: Comp Arch Lectures
In-Reply-To: <20041217173640.49487.qmail@web53807.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20041218032105.B2D0A329DD@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

Posted to ILUGC as a response (of general interest) to a query
about a course based on the following book:

> 
> Reference Book: Hennessy and Patterson, Computer Architecture, A
> Quantitative Approach.
> 
  
The book by Hennessy and Patterson is a classic (though old) and
outlines the basics of the RISC vs. CISC argument, with high
quality profiling metrics and methodology.

  Nowadays, however, the debate in Computer Architecture has
moved far beyond RISC vs. CISC - basically, RISC won the
debate, but it proved to be moot, because all the successful
CISC architectures also adopted the basic RISC design principles,
included single-cycle execution, pipelined execution, 
tight register-to-register data paths, load-store design,
instruction prefetch, etc., thereby nullifying the
advantages of RISC. In the end, x86 (CISC) won in the market,
leaving MIPS, SPARC, ARM, Alpha and POWER (all RISC) with
niche markets measured in small single-digit percentages.

  Most of the interesting work over the last 10 years has moved
into indirect execution (an external CISC instruction set is
decoded on-the-fly into an internal instruction set for a
very different core, usually RISC or VLIW), superscalar
instruction translation/issue, multiple-instruction issue,
indirect VLIW, trace cache optimization, zero-latency execution,
deep-pipeline optimization, etc. Most of this work was done
*after* the Hennessy/Patterson book was written.

  It's just very hard to do any meaningful new design in
that comes close to the efficiency and performance of Kings of
the indirect execution model, i.e. the P6, K7 and K8, all of
which are external CISC x86 and internal RISC superscalar
(they've utterly decimated most of the RISC competition on
a Unit Computation/Unit Energy (MIPS/Watt) basis). Indirect
execution is what has brought us desktop CPUs costing $10
that can do over 1000 MIPS and consume less than 10 W.

  However, the book is still the benchmark 'serious' book
on Computer Architecture today, ~15 years after it was written.
It's a pre-requisite, necessary but insufficient, to do any
serious work in Computer Architecture today. 

  It's also the main reason that all the good work in Computer
Architecture over the last 10 years has moved to Computer
Science (CS), rather than EE-type circuit-theory innovation.

 I'll recommend any introductory course on Computer Architecture
based on this book. 

-Siva (who encountered this book as a whiff of fresh air in 1992,
       after all the crappy 'microprocessor-based design' books
       popular in EE departments)

Totally agree. ARM rockz. Their power management
controller (PMC) is very powerful and flexible. For
example, in AT91 it controls thirty peripheral clocks
and four programmable clocks. It uses four operating
modes Normal, Idle, Slow Clock and Standby operating
modes, which allows us to suspend/resume devices as
and when required.

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Sat Dec 18 11:23:58 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Sat Dec 18 11:53:18 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: [OT] Re: Hennessy and Patterson
In-Reply-To: <20041218044718.GA20809@cs.utexas.edu>
Message-ID: <20041218055358.89DA9329DD@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> > 
> > The book by Hennessy and Patterson is a classic (though old) and
> 
> Old? The third edition is just two years old, and is thoroughly updated to
> contain latest information.
> 
  Necessary and good, because the area has developed rapidly and
well beyond the scope of the original treatment.

> The only reason why indirect execution is necessary is to maintain backward
> compatibility.

  That's the most important reason, commercially; but not the only
one. The main benefit architecturally is that it permits the use of
CISC code-density, reducing the bandwidth requirements on the I-cache
and memory hierarchy. That difference is *huge*, and utterly destroys
the pure RISC contenders.

> One might as well have a true RISC machine like the Alpha
> 21264 or the PowerPC series.

  They've been around for over a decade, and made no headway. The
plug has been pulled on Alpha a few years ago (no further development).
The PowerPC is nice (I've done a fair amount of OS work at IBM on
it), but was never competitive, clock-for-clock, with an x86 of the
same era. It's still around, but with a sub-5% market share. IBM 
pulled the plug on most of the advanced architecture PowerPCs in the
mid-90s. Some good work goes on at Somerset, but Motorola has also
pulled the plug. It simply does not have the criticality to get
beyond this 5% barrier.

> 
> I have not heard this before. I guess the ARM processors which rule the
> embedded world, would rank better as far as power consumption is concerned.
> What is the source from which you have obtained this information?
> 
  We're not talking about power consumption here - there are 4-bit and
8-bit CPUs that consume less than 1 mW, active. We're talking about energy
used for a standard unit of computation, say a complete application
benchmark that involves executing a billion instructions. The figure of
merit here is MIPS/Watt, or Instructions/Watt-Second or Instructions/Joule.
x86 is King of the Hill here, with low-power ULV Pentium III-M and Geode
NX Athlon cores able to perform over 1000 MIPS/Watt, and ARM doesn't
come close. 

  ARM cores are widely-used in the mobile world because they have a small
die and are licensed inexpensively (at a few cents per use), so they're
easy for a third-party fabless company to implement (they're available
as synthesisable soft-cores or hard-cores for a wide variety of processes
as well). It helps that they have low power consumption, but that comes
at a heavy price - poor absolute performance. 

  The reason ARM succeeded in the mobile world is that it is 'good enough'
for the kind of applications originally envisaged to run on cellphones
and PDAs. It ran out of steam for rich media applications like video.
It's pretty pathetic on a pure performance basis, which is why there's
all this nonsensical crap about coprocessors and hardware accelerators
like Jazelle and MPEG HW codecs and so on. x86 moved beyond co-processors
about 2 decades ago. If there's one thing that breaks compatibility and
results in software fragmentation, it's coprocessors. Wanna-be CPUs 
have coprocessors; real CPUs have integrated high-performance datapaths,
usually many of them, with multiple-dispatch. 

  StrongArm (originally DEC, later bought by Intel) is much better on a
performance/Watt basis, but does not scale particularly well beyond about
400-500 MHz. Still, the recent XScale CPUs are pretty impressive but
have not gained much traction beyond PDAs (like the Treo 650).

> My feeling is that H&P is necessary and sufficient. I don't know why you
> say otherwise.
> 
  You can't go out and design a competitive core after reading H&P, but
it will equip you with the foundation to go further. There's been more
than 20 years of development after the original Berkeley and Stanford
RISC work. 

-Siva

--- Sangharsha g  wrote:

=>   What is sata storage!! <=


Please see: http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SATA

SATA interface will replace IDE disk interfaces
in the PC motherboards by 2005.  SATA is pt. to pt.
By the end of 2006 probably IDE disks would become
obsolete and probably won't be offered by major PC
brands.  Dell already ships with certain models of
PC's only with SATA disks.

IMHO, IDE interface will survive only for use
with CD/DVD attach during this period (2005~2006).
Currently, Plextor is the only vendor which offers DVD
burner using SATA interface.

I wouldn't waste my money on IDE products with new
systems after 2004, especially on systems I
intend to use it as a Server.

Hope this helps.

Rudy Colbert

Hi,

Though not want to be seen pedantic
I guess.. perhaps.. you meant 56kbps(7KBps)

It's easy to get confused by transfer rates if not
properly denoted. Usually capital B denotes Byte,
small b denotes bit and supposedly, data communication
standards use a decimal definiton of 1000 bits = 1kbit 
(not 1024 binary stuff). so, 56kbps is actually 7KBps
and KBps is what you read in most applications like
your browser.

If you actually had a 56KBps(448kbps) connection you
would have had no problem downloading ISOs. I know..
Sridhar managed to download "Revolution OS" DVD rip
even through his 64kbps connection.

Kumaraguru

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Sat Dec 18 22:56:57 2004
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Sun Dec 19 12:27:07 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Any Bittorrent users here
In-Reply-To: <e70ef693041218091918ff653b@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20041219065657.2199.qmail@web50202.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi,

--- Srinivasan R <srinivasanr@gmail.com> wrote:
> I downloaded some tutorials, softwares ;-) thru BT
> But I cant dload an entire ISO on my 56KBps
> connection.

Bit torrent is not actually like peer-to-peer file
transfer protocol. It is a different concept. 

Assume we are downloading an iso. The seeds are those
who have the full iso. The seeds distribute chapters
of the iso to the different peers. The peers interact
with each other to get the chapters that they don't
have. In case a peer leaves and the other peers don't
have the chapter yet, you can get it from a seed.

So, you can _always_ stop a bittorrent download and
resume from where you left off.

One of the Internet connections (touchtel) that I use
for downloading isos, I start download at 10 PM and
stop it at 8 AM (free, during this period). I repeat
the same the following day. So, even if the download
doesn't finish in a 10-hour period, I can continue
downloading the next day :)

Regards,

K Shakthi

From rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au  Sun Dec 19 22:54:21 2004
From: rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au (Raja Subramanian)
Date: Sun Dec 19 23:01:19 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Fwd: Comp Arch Lectures
In-Reply-To: <20041218032105.B2D0A329DD@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>
References: <20041217173640.49487.qmail@web53807.mail.yahoo.com>
	<20041218032105.B2D0A329DD@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>
Message-ID: <20041219172421.GA19003@pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au>

Hi,

Sivasankar Chander wrote:
> Posted to ILUGC as a response (of general interest) to a query
> about a course based on the following book:

> > Reference Book: Hennessy and Patterson, Computer Architecture, A
> > Quantitative Approach.

These two books are excellent follow-ons -

    Curt Shimmel: UNIX Systems for Modern Architectures: Symmetric
    Multiprocessing and Caching for Kernel Programmers, Adisson-Wessley.

The focus of this book is on the advanced features of modern CPUs (virtual
memory, caching, smp coherencey, etc) and how they can be used by the
kernel/OS.


Another brilliant one is -

    Charles Severance, Kevin Dowd: High Performance Computing, 2nd Edition
    (Risc Architectures, Optimization & Benchmarks), Oreilly.

This one should be called "The Dummies Guide to HPC" instead!  It's an
_excellent_ read.

Both books assume a solid understanding of computer architecture, and go on to
enlighten the reader on how to write code that exploits the advanced features
on modern CPUs.

- Raja

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Mon Dec 20 12:07:35 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar Babu)
Date: Mon Dec 20 12:06:21 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] installing fedora core from harddisk
In-Reply-To: <341c07aa04121912046d5766b2@mail.gmail.com>
References: <341c07aa04121912046d5766b2@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20041220120735.7d1c9101.lug@chandrashekar.info>

On Mon, 20 Dec 2004 01:34:44 +0530
sathish subramanian <sathish.subramanian@gmail.com> wrote:

> I got FC3 in a DVD. My laptop on which I would Iike to upgrade FC2 to
> FC3 doesnt have a DVD drive. But I have another windows box which has
> DVD drive. So went ahead and shared the DVD drive and is now
> accessible from my laptop. how do i use the shared DVD drive to
> install FC3 in my laptop?

1. Make your Fedora installation packages accessible by one of the
following means:
   a. You can setup a lean webserver/ftp server on your windows box and
copy the contents of FC3 DVD onto the webroot/FTP directory. There's a
README-en file on DVD that will guide you through (about maintaining
directory structure) the process. If you can share your windows folder using NFS
(I'm not sure how, though), you can use that option instead.

   b. Copy the contents of your DVD (from the shared windows box) to a folder in your laptop's windows partition 
(assuming that you do have windows and an extra partition/free space on your laptop to install linux).

2. Boot your laptop using Stage 1 installation CDROM. You can create this CD by burning the boot.iso found within the images/ folder of the DVD, from your windows box. The boot.iso file should be about 5 MB. If your laptop supports booting from a USB pendrive and you do own one, you can write diskboot.img file from the images/ folder onto your pendrive, and try booting from that device on your laptop.

3. After you boot from the Stage 1 installation CDROM, when you are asked about selecting the source media, select the relevant option (HTTP server/FTP/NFS/Mounted hard disk parition) depending on how you setup Step 1.



Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu
http://www.chandrashekar.info/

From joe_steeve at gmx.net  Mon Dec 20 12:30:41 2004
From: joe_steeve at gmx.net (Joe Steeve)
Date: Mon Dec 20 12:07:17 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Fetchmail to fetch only new mails
In-Reply-To: <20041220044136.13639.qmail@web41703.mail.yahoo.com> (Anandh
	G.'s message of "Sun, 19 Dec 2004 20:41:35 -0800 (PST)")
References: <20041220044136.13639.qmail@web41703.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <87mzw9o3mu.fsf@proxy.tcenet>

Anandh G <anandhg02@yahoo.com> writes:
> How to make it to fetch only new mails.

Add a `uidl` before the poll. This will make fetchmail create a
file with the list of message-ids it has already fetched. Note,
pop3 does not make a note of read-unread mails. So, your client
has to do that.

On Mon, 20 Dec 2004 11:47:36 +0530
Karthikeyan <karthikeyan.balasubramanian@aspiresys.com> wrote:


> Actually I want to add more to that.  Is it possible to install linux 
> from DVD
> cd even though I have only VCD player, using something like hardware
> emulation?

No. VCD players can access CDROM media alone. DVD technology is
phenomenally different in ways they are used to store/retrieve
data when compared to CDROM media. Thus a CD drive cannot read DVD.

> Thanks everybody.  Actually one of the reason I asked this question because
> I wanted to download linux iso's and I wanted to find out how best it is
> compared
> to programs like wget or DAP(windows side).  I talked on IRC #mandrake
> list and I found out that it doesnt actually improves speed but it
> actually reduces
> overload on server which allows bittorrent downloads.
> 
> Anybody want to add more.
> 
Actually i could dload files at 6.4kilobytes/sec using Azureus. The
speed is good only if there are many seeds and peers.

This is really fast compared to the speeds of 3-4 I get usually.

If there are no seeders then you cannot dload the file until someone comes up.
You can dload the ISOs from the mirrors using wget or DAP if you find
it is really fast.

From topa_007 at yahoo.com  Mon Dec 20 07:49:37 2004
From: topa_007 at yahoo.com (Toufeeq)
Date: Mon Dec 20 21:19:47 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Jan Meet Talk *Need Feedback*
Message-ID: <20041220154937.73656.qmail@web12702.mail.yahoo.com>

Hello all,

	I was planning a Kernel Talk for the next LUG Meet.

Here is the Topic: Schedulers in Linux 2.6
		*Process Schedulers
		*I/O Schedulers

Here's the breakup of the talk:

I	OS Basics			10mins
	* What is a Scheduler?
	* Process Scheduler Introduction
	* I/O Scheduler
	* Multitasking/Types
		*Co-operative Multitasking
		*Preemptive Multitasking
	
II	Process Scheduler(sched.c)	20 mins
	* Types of Processes
		*CPU bound
		*I/O bound
	* Process Priority
	* Timeslice

III	Scheduling Algorithm		20 mins
	*O(n) Scheduler 2.4 kernel Scheduler
	*O(1) Scheduler 2.6 kernel Scheduler
	*Basic Datastructure for the Scheduler               
          -Runqueue
	*Priority Arrays in the Scheduler
	*Calculating Dynamic Priorities
	*Kernel Preemption and Context Switching

IV	I/O Scheduler Introduction	20 mins
	*Introduction
	*The Elevator Scheduler kernel 2.4 kernel
	*The Anticipatory Scheduler 2.6 kernel
	*The Deadline I/O Scheduler
	*CFQ and Timesliced CFQ Scheduler 2.6.10 ?

TOTAL ~70 mins

I need feedback from the community on the topics
covered and if they 
want any additional topics to be included.

If people feel its too long, I can split the session
into two parts and 
I/O can be discussed on the next week.

Regards,
Toufeeq Hussain

PS: I'm no kernel hacker :), I'll however try to
implement code walkthroughs within the talk.


=====

From raja.mallik at moschip.com  Tue Dec 21 06:38:55 2004
From: raja.mallik at moschip.com (Raja Mallik)
Date: Tue Dec 21 12:08:55 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] File operatins from the kernel
In-Reply-To: <20041220093005.65783.qmail@web54202.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20041220093005.65783.qmail@web54202.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <1103611363.1126.1086.camel@mazda>

Hi chaitanya,

Pl, check out: pl, write your own Makefile: 
works well in 2.4.20-8

Eamaple:

kernelReadFile.c

#define MODULE
#define __KERNEL__
                                                                                                                             
#include <linux/config.h>
#include <linux/module.h>
#include <linux/kernel.h>
#include <linux/fs.h>
/* #include <linux/file.h> */
                                                                                                                             
struct file *fp;
/* MODULE_PARM(file, "s"); */
int init_module()
{
#define BUFF_SIZE 1024
    char buff[BUFF_SIZE];
                                                                                                                             
    fp = filp_open("/proc/devices", O_RDONLY, 0);
    if (IS_ERR(fp)) {
        printk("Opening of file failed! Error: %ld\n", -PTR_ERR(fp));
        return 1;
    }
                                                                                                                             
    memset(buff, 0x00, BUFF_SIZE);
    kernel_read(fp, 0, buff, BUFF_SIZE);
                                                                                                                             
    printk("Buffer: %s\n", buff);
                                                                                                                             
    filp_close(fp, NULL);
   while(1){};
    return 0;
}
                                                                                                                             
void cleanup_module()
{
    ;
}
                                                                                                                             
MODULE_AUTHOR ("raja@xxx.com");
MODULE_DESCRIPTION ("kernelReadfile1");
MODULE_LICENSE ("GPL");

# Block devices
#

# CONFIG_BLK_DEV_XD is not set
# CONFIG_PARIDE is not set
# CONFIG_BLK_CPQ_DA is not set
# CONFIG_BLK_CPQ_CISS_DA is not set
# CONFIG_BLK_DEV_DAC960 is not set

# CONFIG_BLK_DEV_INITRD is not set

# File systems
#

Hi,

Srinivasan Panchabakesan, Ashok (Cognizant) wrote:

>Hi all,
>I am Ashok s p from Chennai.
>Doubt:-
>I want to know how to run "php" web pages in Windows XP system using php , MySql , Apache.
>I have installed "phptraid.exe" from this link http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=9325 <http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=9325&package_id=9390&release_id=75430> &package_id=9390&release_id=75430

Dont use "phptraid".  It can sometimes be pain for configuration.  
Separately download:

* apache
* php5(zip version no exe)
* mysql(zip version no exe)

I tell you it is much easier to configure in winxp.  Just
follow these steps:

1. (apache)

* Install apache(its just an exe), better to choose apache 1.3.28.
* Select custom to change to different folder location i.e C:\Apache

2. (php)

* Extract php5 folder to say C:\php5
* Follow the steps given in install.txt inside php5. I
choose to install as module for apache 1.3.28.  You might have
to add 2 liner in your apache's httpd.conf.


3.

* Extract mysql to say C:\mysql.
* Inside bin directory of mysql double click winmysqladmin.exe
* It will ask for username and password, just give some decent
username and password and you are set.

HTH

Karthikeyan B

From gopu.bhaskar at wipro.com  Tue Dec 21 13:50:42 2004
From: gopu.bhaskar at wipro.com (gopu.bhaskar@wipro.com)
Date: Tue Dec 21 13:51:37 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] RE:File operatins from the kernel
Message-ID: <9FF1E2261921B84C942BD10365DBFC9C020A7606@chn-gdy-msg.wipro.com>




>    I have created a proc entry....and set some values
> to it. I have to check this entry in my module so that
> I can do the appropriate action based on the value of
> this proc entry....So what I need is...how can I
> access this proc entry from the kernel.

Don't know why you are using the proc interface for this, proc interface

Is for user space to look into kernel space.Since you say that _you_
have
created the proc entry, it should be possible for the kernel module to
Set or read the values directly from the other module exported
functions.

Still if you insist, you can use a filp_open call to get the file
struct and then use the member fops struct inside it to do writes and
reads.
The following articles would be good

http://www.cise.ufl.edu/~mfoster/research/kernel/LJArticle.htm
http://www.linux-mag.com/2000-11/gear_01.html


HTH,
Gopu.

Infact vim solves most of the problems for programmers. I have made use of it for almost all of my programming needs. Infact i spend the whole day before a vim-window.

*TIPS*
ctags and vim are the best combination to start off with the Kernel source.

Many useful pluggins for vim are available at http://vim.sourceforge.net

vim can be used as a hexeditor :%!xxd

vim can be used for view difference in multiple files. :help diff

code folding is available :help fold

Split windows are available :help split

a set of quick tips at "http://www.rayninfo.co.uk/vimtips.html"

From asan at lucastvs.co.in  Wed Dec 22 10:51:15 2004
From: asan at lucastvs.co.in (asan@lucastvs.co.in)
Date: Wed Dec 22 10:50:46 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Samba PDC help
Message-ID: <4981F21FF6DA8044A24467205AE7DC6E035572@cadexchange>


>>I am having a PDC running on Samba 3 on FC 2. I have
>>one requirement.
>>I just added samba users by smbpasswd -a. I want samba
>>to change the password of users, if they chage their
>>UNIX password. ie). I want samba to synchronize with
>>UNIX password.
>>Is this possible.

Please enable these lines in your smb.conf,
*************
unix password sync = yes
passwd program = /usr/bin/passwd %u
passwd chat = *Enter\snew\sUNIX\spassword:*\
%n\n *Retype\snew\sUNIX\spassword:* %n\n .
*************

Regards,
Saran

From prabhu_r at users.sourceforge.net  Wed Dec 22 14:27:10 2004
From: prabhu_r at users.sourceforge.net (Prabhu Ramachandran)
Date: Wed Dec 22 14:28:14 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] openafs anyone?
In-Reply-To: <20041221105546.GA4002@pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au>
References: <20041221105546.GA4002@pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au>
Message-ID: <16841.14054.158159.464020@monster.linux.in>

>>>>> "RS" == Raja Subramanian <rsubr@pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au> writes:

    RS> Hi, Has anyone tried distrubuted filesystems such as OpenAFS?
    RS> I'm interested in testing it on a linux/windows network and
    RS> would like to hear about your experiences...

This probably won't help you at all but just gives you a data point.
I looked at it two years ago but decided that it was not worth the
effort.  However, of all the available Distributed File Systems around
OpenAFS seemed like the best bet.  Debian woody already had packages
for OpenAFS that worked at the time.  The trouble was, getting it up
and running and configuring everything to work seemed like a fair bit
of effort.  The docs were good but a bit too verbose IMHO (but verbose
is better than no docs).  My biggest problem was maintenance and
issues with what to do if one of the server disks crashed.  Although
you can have distributed servers and setup a backup server it was too
much to worry about.  Instead I went in for Kerberos for
authentication and used good old NFS for file services.  This was OK
since the setup was for one small lab and not for a real large service
provider.

I haven't checked if anything has changed since then.

cheers,
prabhu

From vallinayagam at ureach.com  Thu Dec 23 04:08:11 2004
From: vallinayagam at ureach.com (V.K.Vallinayagam)
Date: Thu Dec 23 14:38:20 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] My thoughts on introducing linux to newbies
Message-ID: <200412230908.EAA26987@www23.ureach.com>

Hi,
 This is bit long .Read it in leisure.
 Here are some of my thoughts on introducing linux to newbies.
I want to share these thoughts because I see such efforts going
in the form of  the seminars in colleges and Vidyashram efforts
etc. Basically, it suggests how to make it easier for newbies.

Basically when we teach newbies we teach them how
to do basic things in linux.Unlike windows, linux because of
unix heritage has a legacy of some 40 years. ( Assuming  we are
using command line approach than GUI approach ).So naturally
people tend to teach
Shell ( bash shell ), perl, GNU tools like ls, cp, sed awk etc.

 In linux, there are multiple ways and tools to accomplish a
need. Say one may use a combination of sed, awk or instead use
perl or ruby one-liner.Some of the reason for the variety of
tools are, its software development model. More than that, the
timeline. Perl language could not exist in 60's but could grow
in 90's because of processor performance/price improvements.

 From the usage viewpoint, these legacy tools are gradually
losing the marketshare to new tools. Many people use
perl or python or ruby to accomplish something that can be
accomplished by awk. Simply because they don't want to learn
awk. Eric Raymond, articulates this in his book saying that
people don't want to give precious real-estate in their head to
a plethora of special purpose languages and tools when they can
do the same with one generic tool or langage.

 In short, there is a evolution of unix tools and their
adoption.In the 60's people were willing to learn sed, then awk
etc and use shell as the scripting language because the other
option was C language. Now with lavish processing power, people
feel they can be productive with one or few tools and starts
dumping the other tools.Infact in ruby discussion group, people
toy over using ruby shell as the command line shell. There is a
trend of consolidation to few generic tools.

 But most of the times, people who volunteer for free teaching
in terms of classes or writing articles in journals, are kind of
linux veterens that they tend to use legacy tools to accomplish
their need. I used to see articles where the author gives a 3
liner in awk or sed, something like that. The Newbies getting
exposed to that kind of stuff,  gets a feeling that these tools
are essential to learn  and be productive in linux.

 They start learning them. They kind of get a feeling that there
are too many special purpose languages or tools to learn and
feel overwhelmed. Most commands input itself is like a
mini-language. (eg. pstops ). When they fumble using them, like
find tool or awk, they feel inferior that they have not reached
that "expert" or "gurudom" status and that is the problem of
them,  not being productive.

 My suggestion is why pass on the "legacy load" on to the next
generation unnecessarily. Here are some of my thoughts on making
life easier for newbies.

1. A shell with consistent and familiar syntax.
  Bash and bourne-shell are good for normal use. But if one
starts some "if" statements, or loops their syntax is odd. It is
because it inherited the syntax of popular language before 'C' ,
ie Algol. Incase of syntax doubt, try finding the syntax from 
the man page of bash, which runs to 4000 lines. It is a
frustating experience. Most of the times, I end up seeing some
/etc/init.d scripts to refer the syntax rules.
  "rc" shell is better syntactically. It was written first for
plan 9 . It is written to address this problem. It is lot easier
for the head.

2. A scripting language that is good in string handling instead
of sed,awk,tr, cut etc.
   Infact shell itself is a scripting language.It was the only
scripting language available then, so piping using these tools
was the favourite then. ( from 70's .. )
   My preferences are in the decling order are.
   1. TCL
   2. Ruby
   3. Python
   4. Perl

   It is difficult to tell all the benefits of TCL here, very
simple syntax that borders with shell, but has the capabities of
other language. etc. But somehow it went out of people's radar
after mid 90's.

   Ruby for neat object orientation.After using the iterators,
code-blocks,  doing loops in other languages seems so painful.

  Again time-line comes here, Ruby developed in '95 became
popular some 2 years before. Python was before that. Perl around
88. Thus object-orientation is more good in ruby.

 They say unix principle is KISS, ie keep it simple stupid. No
one will say unix commands like "find", "ls" are simple.
Meaning, one cannot keep all their options and functions in
their  head. In that sense the functions of the scripting
languages follow the "KISS" principle. Part of the reasons
being, shell as a language is limited in flexibility so
complexibity is moved to the components . 
 I don't say  we should not use these commands. My
recommendation for newbies is use it for simple uses for
anything beyond, go to a scripting language. It (complex Unix
commands and optinos) is not worth learning to use them for
complex needs. That was needed in 60's not now. 

Regards
V.K.Vallinayagam
From gopalarathnam_v at yahoo.com  Thu Dec 23 14:54:17 2004
From: gopalarathnam_v at yahoo.com (Gopalarathnam V.)

V.K.Vallinayagam wrote:
> a plethora of special purpose languages and tools when they can
> do the same with one generic tool or langage.

IMO there is no one-general purpose tool for everything, even 
Perl/Python/whatever is not panacea.

> 
> frustating experience. Most of the times, I end up seeing some
> /etc/init.d scripts to refer the syntax rules.
>   "rc" shell is better syntactically. It was written first for
> plan 9 . It is written to address this problem. It is lot easier
> for the head.

Is it? whatever thats easy for me is not easy for everybodyelse! I heard 
a couple of my friends say C++ is easier than PHP!!

> 
>  They say unix principle is KISS, ie keep it simple stupid. No
> one will say unix commands like "find", "ls" are simple.
> Meaning, one cannot keep all their options and functions in
> their  head. In that sense the functions of the scripting

(One of) Unix principle is one program does only one thing and does that 
well.  The purpose of "ls" is to list files, "find" to find files, 
directories, etc. Thats where filters, pipes, come in to the picture.

>>
>> Is it? whatever thats easy for me is not easy for everybodyelse! I

>> a couple of my friends say C++ is easier than PHP!!
> He is saying that from the ignorance of dynamic languages .. tell him
> to learn Python first and compare that with C++ .....

To set the background and my credentials and biases:
my language route was BASIC, COBOL, C, Clipper, sh scripts, awk, C++, 
Python, Java
And I have written production code in all of them (probably totalling 
200,000 lines)
My firm favourite is Python.

And I find myself in sympathy with the sentiment 'C++ is easier than 
PHP'
I could not easily relate to perl and php for very similar reasons. I 
am very uncomfortable with
languages where variables sport $s etc., In fact I found it difficult 
to learn Lisp and Dylan for similar reasons.
Despite infectious enthusiasm of some PHP experts (Cheeni and Suraj), 
and absolute demolition jobs by perl expert(BGa)
  I found it difficult to cross the $ barrier in PHP and perl; and I 
found ruby heavy going too.

In fact I find it even difficult these days to deal tolerantly with the 
braces of C/C++/Java.
I believe that many people who like python, do so for  its simplicity 
and its use of white space,
while the majority of those who dislike it do so for the same reason: 
white space!!

My advice:
	1. Do not restrict yourself to a single language.
	2. Write or read decent amount of code in one language from
the C/C++ group
	3. then try Java;
	4. then learn Python or Ruby.
	5. Then take a look at as many of the following
		Dylan		Lisp
		Scala		Scheme
		oCaml		Mozart
	
I hope to l talk about the functional programming aspects of Python and 
my dabblings in Scala and Dylan some time.
  		
Asokan Pichai
---------------------
If you are a fresher interested in effective career options
take a look at http://www.mafoiacademy.com

From kums at gmx.net  Thu Dec 23 18:57:52 2004
From: kums at gmx.net (Kumaraguru)
Date: Thu Dec 23 18:58:11 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Header set Server - Apache 
References: <20041223114819.75424.qmail@web51710.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <001c01c4e8f3$36a4bf40$0d07a8c0@kums>

1) The Header directives are processed just before the response
is sent by its handler. These means that some headers that are
added just before the response is sent and cannot be unset or
overridden. This includes headers such as "Date" and "Server". 
http://httpd.apache.org/docs/mod/mod_headers.html 


2) How can I change the information that Apache returns about
itself in the headers? 
Frequently, people want to remove this information, under the
mistaken understanding that this will make the system more secure.
This is probably not the case, as the same exploits will likely be
attempted regardless of the header information you provide.
http://httpd.apache.org/docs/misc/FAQ.html#serverheader
There are, however, two answers to this question: the correct answer,
and the answer that you are probably looking for....


3) ServerTokens directive - This directive controls whether
 Server response header field which is sent back to clients
 includes a description of the generic OS-type of the server
 as well as information about compiled-in modules. 
 http://httpd.apache.org/docs/mod/core.html#servertokens

> efforts going

> Vidyashram efforts

You are making a false assumption that it was _only_
for newbies. 

Also, one cannot teach kernel programming to newbies
who haven't had a taste of user-space. And if you are
going to work in kernel space, you will need to
understand the use of Makefiles and scripts in
user-space. Getting to learn scripting is only a start
:)

saravanan ganapathy wrote:
> Other Config which I did was 
>   ServerSignature Off, Run Apache as non-root user
> without shell access

Redundant.  Apache starts as root but always forks as an unprivileged user

> Any other tips to secure apache?

Dont worry about the security of apache

Worry about -

1. Security of the php / cgi etc scripts you are running on that server 
(poke around for security advisories on formmail, gallery etc .. and 
read up on how to write secure cgi and php scripts)

2. Security / settings on the apache modules you run - mod_proxy or 
mod_php4 for example

> (my idea is instead of broadcast everything, we can
> secure as much possible)

You've got a whole lot of wrong ideas, amigo ..

From rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au  Thu Dec 23 23:14:59 2004
From: rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au (Raja Subramanian)
Date: Thu Dec 23 23:23:00 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] [Iligc] IMAP mail to POP3 conversion
In-Reply-To: <41CA9BA4.000003.27705@SRL>
References: <41CA9BA4.000003.27705@SRL>
Message-ID: <20041223174459.GA31430@pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au>

Hi,

Shankar Lakshmanan wrote:
> I have an IMAP server which has a lot of user mailboxes and mail which the
> users read through their Netscape mail clients on Windoze. However, some
> users want their mails moved from the server to their client machines so
> that they can read their mails (through Netscape POP3 clients) even when the
> IMAP server is down. . Any pointers to whether this can be done ? Right now,
> they are able to see only  the mail subject headers without the text bodies
> 

IMAP itself supports disconnected operation.  You mail client should have an
option like "make available for offline use".  Enable that and then sync with
the imap server and you will be downloading the message bodies as well.

Most IMAP clients can do a full two-way sync, so you can sync the same mailbox
mail from your home and office PC.

- Raja

From gopalarathnam_v at yahoo.com  Thu Dec 23 23:22:16 2004
From: gopalarathnam_v at yahoo.com (Gopalarathnam V.)
Date: Fri Dec 24 12:52:24 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Problem in Extracting an archive
In-Reply-To: <20041224071616.12633.qmail@webmail32.rediffmail.com>
Message-ID: <20041224072216.37830.qmail@web52207.mail.yahoo.com>

tar -xf archive-name

Read tar --help, or man tar.
But, I suspect that the archive might be a gzipped
tarball because on some browsers use wrong file
extension when saving, so probably what you have
should be a filename.tar.gz.
In that case, use
tar -xzf archive-name.

Check the file type using the file command.

From eprasanna at touchtelindia.net  Thu Dec 23 22:06:48 2004
From: eprasanna at touchtelindia.net (ePrasanna)
Date: Fri Dec 24 15:38:04 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Connecting two computers
In-Reply-To: <da6a4312041223022049d1da42@mail.gmail.com>
References: <da6a4312041223022049d1da42@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <41CAF420.2040505@touchtelindia.net>

Ganesh V wrote:

>Hi! 
>  
>    I have two comps. One running FC3 and another running Debian sid.
>I need to transfer files between them and I have Ethernet cards ( on
>both comps) and a cable connecting both those ports. What should I do
>to achieve the connection. I configured both their networks cards and
>then I fixed their IP addresses to 10.133.1.5 and 10.13.1.6. What do I
>do for the other parameters like their DNS server names, Subnet mask
>etc.
>
>Any pointers!!! 
>
>Bye!
>
>  
>
Hi,

 1> Ensure that u use a ethernet_cross_cable to connect both the 
computers, and plug them directly into the NICs. Next ensure that 
atleast one PC is configured to be 10Mbps, leaving both the cards to 
auto_negotiate will give you problems sometimes. Its always better to 
start with the lowest config (10Mbps/Half Duplex) and then try fiddling 
with various options and settle at the highest config that works for 
you. And keep the length of the cable less than 100 meters gives you 
better performance.

2> Is the network 10.133.1.5 and 10.13.1.6, if so you shd use the 
netmask as 255.0.0.0. If its 10.13.1.5 and 10.13.1.6, then you can use 
255.255.255.0 as the netmask. No need of DNS and Gateway IPs.

3> For more info on IP addressing, pls check some of the Internetworking 
articles on www.cisco.com and NAG / SAG on www.tldp.org.

ePrasanna

On Sat, 25 Dec 2004 08:42:52 +0530, Krishnaswamy Subramanian
<krishnaswamy84@gmail.com> wrote:
> Hi
> 
>             I am interested in GUI programming in linux but I don't know
> where to start can anybody suggest me the books to be referred and where to
> start with
> 

There are many GUI toolkits in Linux, the most popular (possibly the
best) ones are

1. GTK+ - http://gtk.org - LGPL (C)
2. WxWidgets (C++) - http://wxwidgets.org/
3. QT - GPL (C++)

GNOME uses GTK+ and KDE uses Qt.  Both the toolkits has bindings for
many languages, means you can use then for any language you choose,
except that Qt has no C version (as it is written in C++).  WxWidgets
is known to be buggy.  GTK+ apps does not look very great under
Windows, but they come close (eg. Curve theme in Gaim Windows).

You can start from here
http://gtk.org/tutorial

For python GUI programming, see 
http://pygtk.org
http://wxwidgets.org/

IMO, GTK+ is a lot more easier to learn/use than other toolkits.

TODO: put this in the wiki :)

-- 
Sridhar R - http://cs.annauniv.edu/~rsridhar
Blog: http://www.livejournal.com/~sridharinfinity

"buggy", no idea what version of wxWindows/wxWidgets you are talking
of.  

I've used wxPython to do fairly non-trivial things, like write a
cross-platform electromagnetics visualization package using wxPython.
This was circa 2001 -- which is quite a long while ago.  I also happen
to know how poor GTK+/gtkmm was way back in 1998.  At that time there
was no choice between KDE/Gnome -- it had to be KDE.  GTK+ has had a
huge face-lift since version-2.0.  However, it is still not the choice
for completely cross platform GUI development.  That does not warrant
a statement to the effect that "GTK+ is known to be buggy"!  :)

Right now GTK has matured vastly and the widgets are really nice.
PyGTK has almost always been extremely well maintained and developed.
I'll also agree that GTK it is the one toolkit that probably has the
largest Linux mindshare (along with Qt) and probably has the most
number of supported languages.  However, if someone wants to deploy an
application across platforms (read: if significant fraction of your
users use win32) then I'm not sure GTK+ is even today a good choice.
Qt is a pain because of its license but from what I've heard its an
awesome framework to work with.  The big deal about wxWidgets is that
applications written with it look "native" on each platform, for some
folks this is very important.

The choice of toolkit also depends on your personal programming
preferences.  If you really like all the typecasts in C, and hate C++
you'd definitely pick GTK+ over Qt or wxWidgets.  OTOH, if you like
C++ its unlikely you'll enjoy GTK+.  I don't know how gtkmm has
matured to comment on how good it is today.  Some people prefer FLTK
to all the other alternatives.

As with anything, you need to know what you need and pick the right
set of tools.  Blanket statements of the "bugginess" of toolkits are
IMNSHO meaningless.  There are horror stories on either side of the
fence. 

So in summary, all the mentioned toolkits are usable.  Each has its
strengths and weaknesses.  Do your research, find out what you need
and use the suitable tool.  Unfortunately, there isn't one tool that
does "everything" today.

cheers,
prabhu

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Sun Dec 26 20:08:06 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Sun Dec 26 20:37:40 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] OT: Automated Tsunami warning script/program ?
Message-ID: <20041226143806.CA589329E0@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>


  Just thinking out aloud - it should be fairly trivial to develop a
PHP/Perl script that parses the USGS Earthquake Hazards site at
http://earthquakes.usgs.gov, retrieves information for all earthquake
events, and automatically sends out an e-mail alarm when an event
exceeding a certain magnitude (say 7.0) occurs within a well-defined
Oceanic region (say the Indian Ocean / Bay of Bangal). This would
be similar to the systems already in operation at the Pacific
Tsunami Watch Centre (PTWC) at Honolulu, Hawaii and the Alaska
Tsunami Watch Centre (ATWC), both of which parse a network of
seismometers and issue automated warnings.

  The reason this works very well for the US and Japan is that
the Pacific Ocean is fairly large, so there's a sufficient
delay between an Earthquake event (which can be detected in
less than 15 minutes around the globe from the fast-propagating
P-Wave) and the following Tsunami, which could take about 12 hours
to get from one side of the Pacific Ocean to the other. This allows
ample time for a warning to be circulated.

  In the case of the Great Sumatran/Andamans Earthquake of 2004
(which took place this morning), the P-wave would have reached Madras
in about 4 minutes, while the Tsunami took about 2.5-3 hours to reach
Madras.

The time difference would have been barely sufficient to get a
message out on the Radio/TV and evacuate the low-lying coastal areas.
Difficult, but definitely well within reach of present technology.
However, it's another issue whether we have the civic discipline
to actually perform an orderly and timely evacuation in India :-(.

-Siva

Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Automated Tsunami warning script
In-Reply-To: <41CF8280.6050108@frodo.hserus.net>
Message-ID: <20041227041627.60FFF329E0@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> so its not just a simple matter of perl / python scripting
> you need a good local source of alerts.
> 
> -------- Original Message --------
> Subject: Re: [Fwd: [Ilugc] OT: Automated Tsunami warning script/program ?]
> Date: Mon, 27 Dec 2004 11:21:31 +0800
> From: James Lick <jlick@drivel.com>
> 
> I have a script to pull data for Taiwan from the Central Weather Bureau
> web site: http://jameslick.com/twquake/
> 
> I also send out automated email warnings in English and Chinese of
> quakes here:
> http://www.tcp.com/mailman/listinfo/twquake-alert-en
> http://www.tcp.com/mailman/listinfo/twquake-alert-zh
> 
> It would be possible to make a similiar script to pull from USGS,
> however, they are fairly slow to post quake info for international
> quakes, sometimes an hour or two after they happen.  For example, with
> yesterday's great quake the first email notification was sent out by
> USGS an hour and 19 minutes after in occurred and wasn't received by my
> mail server until 3 minutes later.  This is a pretty typical delay with
> USGS reporting.  So it would be a poor source of data to make warnings
> from.  I mainly haven't done a script for them because they already have
> a good mailing list and they are too slow to be useful for international
> quakes.
> 
> Taiwan's CWB typically posts information within 5 minutes of a quake,
> and I poll for new data every 10 minutes for posting to the mailing
> lists, so it would be a much more timely source of data. 
> 
Thanks SRS, Jim for the info.

I noticed that the USGS site had a time
lag, but it has the most accurate triangulation. Also, they have
automated e-mail notifications, but they have too much latency (hours
to days) to be useful (as Jim noted).

The International Tsunami Information Center (ITIC), Pacific Tsunami
Watch Center (PTWC) and the Alaska Tsunami Watch Center (ATWC) also
had bulletins describing the quake and rather bland 'no risk
to the Pacific area' and 'possible local Tsunami' observations. In
retrospect, rather accurate but ineffectual, since none of the bulletins
were forwarded to the respective regions that were most at risk.

The 2.5 hour lag between this quake and the Tsunami was certainly
sufficient to get a warning out, even if very few had actually heeded
it. There's nobody alive today who was born in 1883, when the last
Tsunami hit Madras (that was a meagre 1-m swell from the explosion
of Krakatoa volcano in Indonesia).

I also observed that the USGS has updated the name of the earthquake
to the Great Andaman/Nicobar earthquake, probably because most of the
aftershocks and slippage seem to be happening there - there are a
few aftershocks pretty close to Burma/Bangladesh also, and events
are still unfolding. The Tsunami risk has probably receded now,
although another magnitude 7-8 aftershock can still not be ruled out.

-Siva

Hi List,
  I am using qmail + SMTP Auth + rblsmtpd.  Some users are not able to
send mails since they are blocked in rbl list. But they are valid
users. RBL checking is taking place before SMTP AUTH. so the client
got rejected.
  Is there any way to use SMTP AUTH first and RBL next.

exec /usr/local/bin/softlimit -m 19000000 \
    /usr/local/bin/tcpserver -v -R -l "$LOCAL" -x /etc/tcp.smtp.cdb -c
"$MAXSMTPD" \
        -u "$QMAILDUID" -g "$NOFILESGID" 0 smtp \
        /usr/local/bin/rblsmtpd -r relays.ordb.org \
        -r bl.spamcop.net -r list.dsbl.org -r sbl.spamhaus.org \
        -r korea.services.net -r dnsbl.sorbs.net \
        /var/qmail/bin/qmail-smtpd \
        mydomain.com /var/vpopmail/bin/vchkpw /bin/true 2>&1


Regards
Moorthy
From linux at frodo.hserus.net  Wed Dec 29 10:26:04 2004
From: linux at frodo.hserus.net (Suresh Ramasubramanian)
Date: Wed Dec 29 10:26:01 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] qmail+smtp auth+rblsmtpd
References: <1cc2ae1041228204649994695@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <02e601c4ed62$b4b427e0$1601a8c0@hserus.net>


Narayanamoorthy Srinivasan <narayanamoorthys@gmail.com> wrote:
>  Is there any way to use SMTP AUTH first and RBL next.

1. Patch qmail

or

2. Run a separate instance of qmail on port 587, and dont run rblsmtpd 
on it - limit access to this qmail instance only to smtp auth'd users, 
and to IPs that are in your dialup pool / LAN etc (IPs that you normally 
relay for)

    srs

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Tue Dec 28 23:58:11 2004
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Wed Dec 29 13:28:20 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] File operations from kernel
In-Reply-To: <BAY23-F966E6EA0334C2BD877165BA9B0@phx.gbl>
