Hi Chaitanya:

--- chaitanya valluru <csvalluru@hotmail.com> wrote:
>    create one /proc directory "ser_eth" and one
> entry in it..."s_e"....which 
> is of type char *.

... in the driver.
 
>   If "s_e" is set to "YES" , I have to load another
> module.

Use request_module,

int request_module(const char *module_name);

Chapter 11: kmod and Advanced Modularization:
http://www.xml.com/ldd/chapter/book/ch11.html

>   I have associated read and write procedures to
> this entry. I used the 
> "char *page" parameter of these procedures to read
> and write the 
> value.....

This is from kernel space, in the driver.

> But I am not getting the result.i.e. I
> couldn't read from or write 
> to the correct values into the entry....

/proc is read-only.
 
> Can anyone help me out, as to how this can be
> done...i.e.,to read and 
> write the values of proc entry from within the
> procedures itself..

This value is stored in the driver itself. Depending
on the value (YES/NO), you can do the appropriate
function in the driver. You don't need /proc itself.

From kdeepakin at yahoo.com  Wed Dec 29 07:41:57 2004
From: kdeepakin at yahoo.com (Deepak K)
Date: Wed Dec 29 21:12:05 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Connecting two computers
In-Reply-To: <da6a4312041228223258a204ef@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20041229154157.3867.qmail@web50909.mail.yahoo.com>

Ganesh,

If the socket resembles as of telephone jack and
slightly bigger, it is a RJ45 a standard to connect
ethernet nodes. 

if you are just having two computers and would like do
data transfer you need to have cross-over cable
ethernet cable with RJ45 at both ends. 

if you do not have cross over cable, then,  you can
introduce a hub .the basic function of a simple hub is
to repeat the signals that it gets . i.e., it
amplifies the signal and nothing else.  you should
find a normal hub in every place of your computer lab.
the hub will have number of ports on its front side to
accept the RJ45 mentioned above. 

take two RJ45 cable and connect both the computers to
the hub. now try pinging or ssh .

--deepak--

Subject: [Ilugc] qmail+smtp auth+rblsmtpd

Suresh,

qmail with RBL is  reactive spam solution.  hence, a
email submission has to happen followed by RBL
rule/lookup execution.

hence, smtp auth will happen first, the email will be
submitted to the queue and then RBL rule/lookup
exectuion would happen. 

Regards
K.Deepak

Deepak K wrote:
> qmail with RBL is  reactive spam solution.  hence, a
> email submission has to happen followed by RBL
> rule/lookup execution.

The problem is that he is using rblsmtpd.. so what happens is when 
there's an smtp connect from a blocked IP, it will open into an rblsmtpd 
daemon, which does nothing except issue a 5xx reject and close the 
connection

So running qmail on an alternate port for submission users is an idea ..

	srs

> > But I am not getting the result.i.e. I

> /proc is read-only.
> 

/proc is not read-only. There are many operations that can be done by
writing to the proc fs. Setting console log level, adding scsi devices,
disabling the magic SysRq key, to name a few. Just like the read
corresponding callback funtion there is one for writing too.
The following link might help

http://www.kernelnewbies.org/documents/kdoc/procfs-guide/lkprocfsguide.h
tml

Gopu Bhaskar.

From vijairaj_sr at rediffmail.com  Thu Dec 30 08:30:07 2004
From: vijairaj_sr at rediffmail.com (Vijairaj  R)
Date: Thu Dec 30 14:00:09 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Connecting two computers
Message-ID: <20041230083104.30525.qmail@webmail45.rediffmail.com>


On Wed, 29 Dec 2004 Ganesh V wrote :
>I don't understand what is meant by a hub.

When signals travel through the cable, over a distance, the voltage level reduces and beyond certain length it would not be possible to distinguish between 0's and 1's. Hub is a device connected to the cable before this critical length so that it restores the voltage levels.

When two computers are connected directly, the 'Send' pin of one computer should be connected to the 'receive' of the other, Cross over cables are used to achieve just this.


>I will try out all the subnet masks possible and

IMHO, its a waste of time. Don't just waste your time trying randomly all possible values. Instead understand the underlying concept and arrive at the best possible value. The time spent in understanding is worth it - You would have finally saved a lot of time.

I have seen people doing this sort of random manipulation, this is especially hazardous is the linux world. Enter one wrong command and you are easily in trouble.

--
Regards
R. Vijairaj

SRS, I think you got me wrong. I meant *any* random manipulation, not limited to subnet mask alone, is a bad way of doing things and yes this holds good for whatever OS.

I meant that one can easily harm oneself by running a command without knowing what it does. 

I was of the view that one should know what he does and should be prepared for the outcome.

-- A little OT --
I wanted to stress this point because i have seen people using debuggers to decide the logic. When a program doesn't work they just substitute various values (random manipulation) and finally arrive at the required result. This is not the right way. Debuggers are used to find the bugs and not to fix it and should be used only at extreme cases.

From gopu.bhaskar at wipro.com  Thu Dec 30 17:49:52 2004
From: gopu.bhaskar at wipro.com (gopu.bhaskar@wipro.com)
Date: Thu Dec 30 17:50:49 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: File operations from kernel
Message-ID: <9FF1E2261921B84C942BD10365DBFC9C02198778@chn-gdy-msg.wipro.com>



> > /proc is not read-only. There are many operations
> > that can be done by
> > writing to the proc fs.
>
> Isn't this a little complicated?
>
> "Fully featured /proc entries can be complicated
> beasts; among other things, they can be written to as
> well as read from. Most of the time, however, /proc
> entries are read-only files"

So does Alessandro Rubinis quote mean that "/proc is read-only." ?
/proc fs I reiterate is _not_ read only. They are read only, only when
the write is not implemented. Chaitanyas question was clear, he needed
help with writing and reading in proc fs.

>
> http://www.xml.com/ldd/chapter/book/ch04.html#t2
>
> Using ioctl(), read(), write() can be readily used and
> are quite simple for transferring data/commands to the
> driver.

Kernel modules can be written for a lot of other purposes than device
drivers. One cannot go about registering a device whenever he needs to
interface with user land.

Btb Chaithanya never said that he is writing a device driver, he only
said that he has to write a kernel module. Doing something like 'echo
"YES" > /proc/ser_eth/s_e' would be easier for a _user_ to do, much
better than forcing the user to open the device and calling an ioctl.

Also I don't feel implementing a write/read in proc is that difficult.
Please read the following link which is an sample implementation.

http://lxr.linux.no/source/Documentation/DocBook/procfs_example.c

In my opinion using proc fs is better for simple operations like this.

Happy 2005 to all.

Gopu Bhaskar.

> I just wanted to know if anyone has succesfully configured the USB
> modem that comes along
> with the airtel DSL connection. I just bought the connection a week
> back and it works great on windows, but i am unable to use the modem
> in linux. I use Mandrake Linux 10.1 community edition.

Hi Vishnu, you need to start by finding out what
chipset your modem uses.  I dont have the same modem
as you have.  Mine is a Zyxel Prestige 630-11.

If you run the same chipset as this modem (Alcatel
Dynamite Chipset MTC-20158) then you are in business.
Get to http://sourceforge.net/projects/zyxel630-11/
and download the source code and you would be in
business.  

I am running Redhat 9.  I had to do a few more things:
 update modtools, update my ppd daemon to support PPoA.

I have configured qmail qmqpd server in redhat 9 and
its working fine.

I have setup TCP service for qmqpd:
[root@server1 control]# vi /etc/tcprules.d/qmqp.tcp
Add the lines:
207.150.162.120:allow
:deny
Converted /etc/tcprules.d/qmqp.tcp to tcprules
/etc/tcprules.d/qmqp.cdb :
[root@server1 control]# tcprules
/etc/tcprules.d/qmqp.cdb /etc/tcprules.d/qmqp.tmp <
/etc/tcprules.d/qmqp.tcp 
I have started the qmail-qmqpd service as: 
[root@server1 control]# tcpserver -x
/etc/tcprules.d/qmqp.cdb -u 102 -g 102 0 628
/var/qmail/bin/qmail-qmqpd &


But, I want to make this rule automatically run during
each time the system is booted.
Can any one of you help..


thank you,
